      <p><b>Armenia</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Armenia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/46/En-us-Armenia.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Armenia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">Հայաստան</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Armenian" title="Romanization of Armenian">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="hy-Latn" title="Armenian-language romanization">Hayastan</i>, <small>IPA:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Armenian" title="Help:IPA/Armenian">[hɑjɑsˈtɑn]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Armenia</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[a]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Highlands" title="Armenian Highlands">Armenian Highlands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-classification_of_world_regions_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-classification_of_world_regions-16">[15]</a></sup> It is a part of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> region; and is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> to the north, the <a href="/wiki/Lachin_corridor" title="Lachin corridor">Lachin corridor</a> under a <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_ceasefire_agreement" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh ceasefire agreement">Russian peacekeeping force</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> to the east, and <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and the Azerbaijani <a href="/wiki/Exclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclave">exclave</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nakhchivan_Autonomous_Republic" title="Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic">Nakhchivan</a> to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-Oxford_University_Press_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford_University_Press-18">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Armenia is a unitary, multi-party, democratic <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">nation-state</a> with an ancient cultural heritage. The first Armenian state of <a href="/wiki/Urartu" title="Urartu">Urartu</a> was established in 860 BC, and by the 6th century BC it was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Satrapy_of_Armenia" title="Satrapy of Armenia">Satrapy of Armenia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Armenia_(antiquity)" title="Kingdom of Armenia (antiquity)">Kingdom of Armenia</a> reached its height under <a href="/wiki/Tigranes_the_Great" title="Tigranes the Great">Tigranes the Great</a> in the 1st century BC and became the first state in the world to adopt <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> as its <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">official religion</a> in the late 3rd or early 4th century AD.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> The official date of state adoption of Christianity is 301.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> The ancient Armenian kingdom was split between the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanian Empires</a> around the early 5th century. Under the <a href="/wiki/Bagratuni_dynasty" title="Bagratuni dynasty">Bagratuni dynasty</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bagratid_Kingdom_of_Armenia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bagratid Kingdom of Armenia">Bagratid Kingdom of Armenia</a> was restored in the 9th century. Declining due to the wars against the Byzantines, the kingdom fell in 1045 and Armenia was soon after invaded by the <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_Empire" title="Seljuk Empire">Seljuk Turks</a>. An Armenian principality and later a kingdom <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Kingdom_of_Cilicia" title="Armenian Kingdom of Cilicia">Cilician Armenia</a> was located on the coast of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> between the 11th and 14th centuries. </p>
      <p>Between the 16th and 19th centuries, the traditional Armenian homeland composed of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Armenia" title="Eastern Armenia">Eastern Armenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Armenia" title="Western Armenia">Western Armenia</a> came under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian Empire">Persian</a> empires, repeatedly ruled by either of the two over the centuries. By the 19th century, Eastern Armenia had been conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, while most of the western parts of the traditional Armenian homeland remained under Ottoman rule. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, 1.5 million Armenians living in their ancestral lands in the Ottoman Empire were systematically exterminated in the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian Genocide</a>. In 1918, following the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a>, all non-Russian countries declared their independence after the Russian Empire ceased to exist, leading to the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Armenia" title="First Republic of Armenia">First Republic of Armenia</a>. By 1920, the state was incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasian_Socialist_Federative_Soviet_Republic" title="Transcaucasian Socialist Federative Soviet Republic">Transcaucasian Socialist Federative Soviet Republic</a>, and in 1922 became a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. In 1936, the Transcaucasian state was dissolved, transforming its constituent states, including the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic">Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, into full <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">Union republics</a>. The modern Republic of Armenia became independent in 1991 during the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>. </p>
      <p>Armenia is a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a> and ranks 81st on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (2018).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Armenia" title="Economy of Armenia">economy</a> is primarily based on industrial output and mineral extraction. While Armenia is geographically located in the South Caucasus, it is generally considered <a href="/wiki/Geopolitically" class="mw-redirect" title="Geopolitically">geopolitically</a> European. Since Armenia aligns itself in many respects geopolitically with <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, the country is a member of numerous European organizations including the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Partnership" title="Eastern Partnership">Eastern Partnership</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurocontrol" title="Eurocontrol">Eurocontrol</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_European_Regions" title="Assembly of European Regions">Assembly of European Regions</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="European Bank for Reconstruction and Development">European Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a>. Armenia is also a member of certain regional groups throughout <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organization" title="Collective Security Treaty Organization">Collective Security Treaty Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurasian Union">Eurasian Union</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Development_Bank" title="Eurasian Development Bank">Eurasian Development Bank</a>. Armenia supports the <i>de facto</i> independent <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh">Artsakh</a>, which was proclaimed in 1991. Armenia also recognises the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic Church</a>, the world's oldest <a href="/wiki/National_church" title="National church">National church</a>, as the country's primary religious establishment.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Article_18_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Article_18-4">[4]</a></sup> The unique <a href="/wiki/Armenian_alphabet" title="Armenian alphabet">Armenian alphabet</a> was created by <a href="/wiki/Mesrop_Mashtots" title="Mesrop Mashtots">Mesrop Mashtots</a> in 405 AD. </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Armenia" title="Name of Armenia">Name of Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The original native <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a> name for the country was <span lang="hy" title="Armenian-language text">Հայք</span> (<i><i lang="hy-Latn" title="Armenian-language text"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D5%80%D5%A1%D5%B5%D6%84" class="extiw" title="wikt:Հայք">Hayk’</a></i></i>); however, it is currently rarely used. The contemporary name <span lang="hy" title="Armenian-language text">Հայաստան</span> (<i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D5%80%D5%A1%D5%B5%D5%A1%D5%BD%D5%BF%D5%A1%D5%B6" class="extiw" title="wikt:Հայաստան">Hayastan</a></i>) became popular in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> by addition of the <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> suffix <i><a href="/wiki/-stan" title="-stan">-stan</a></i> (place).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. However the origins of the name Hayastan trace back to much earlier dates and were first attested in circa 5th century in the works of <a href="/wiki/Agathangelos" title="Agathangelos">Agathangelos</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Faustus_of_Byzantium" title="Faustus of Byzantium">Faustus of Byzantium</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ghazar_Parpetsi" title="Ghazar Parpetsi">Ghazar Parpetsi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Koryun" class="mw-redirect" title="Koryun">Koryun</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sebeos" title="Sebeos">Sebeos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The name has traditionally been derived from <a href="/wiki/Hayk" title="Hayk">Hayk</a> (<span lang="hy" title="Armenian-language text">Հայկ</span>), the legendary patriarch of the <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a> and a great-great-grandson of <a href="/wiki/Noah" title="Noah">Noah</a>, who, according to the 5th-century AD author <a href="/wiki/Moses_of_Chorene" class="mw-redirect" title="Moses of Chorene">Moses of Chorene (Movsis Khorenatsi)</a>, defeated the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Kings_of_Babylon" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Kings of Babylon">Babylonian king</a> Bel in <a href="/wiki/3rd_millennium_BC" title="3rd millennium BC">2492&nbsp;BC</a> and established his nation in the <a href="/wiki/Ararat,_Armenia" title="Ararat, Armenia">Ararat</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> The further origin of the name is uncertain. It is also further postulated<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bauer_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bauer-34">[33]</a></sup> that the name <i>Hay</i> comes from one of the two confederated, Hittite vassal states&nbsp;– the <a href="/wiki/Hayasa" class="mw-redirect" title="Hayasa">Ḫayaša</a>-Azzi (1600–1200 BC). </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Exonym_and_endonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Exonym and endonym">exonym</a> <i>Armenia</i> is attested in the <a href="/wiki/Old_Persian" title="Old Persian">Old Persian</a> <a href="/wiki/Behistun_Inscription" title="Behistun Inscription">Behistun Inscription</a> (515 BC) as <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%F0%90%8E%A0%F0%90%8E%BC%F0%90%8E%B7%F0%90%8E%A1%F0%90%8E%B4#Old_Persian" class="extiw" title="wikt:𐎠𐎼𐎷𐎡𐎴">Armina</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/File:Old_Persian_a.png" class="image"><img alt="Old Persian a.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Old_Persian_a.png/20px-Old_Persian_a.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Old_Persian_a.png/30px-Old_Persian_a.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Old_Persian_a.png/40px-Old_Persian_a.png 2x" data-file-width="184" data-file-height="184"></a> <a href="/wiki/File:Old_Persian_ra.png" class="image"><img alt="Old Persian ra.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Old_Persian_ra.png/20px-Old_Persian_ra.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Old_Persian_ra.png/30px-Old_Persian_ra.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Old_Persian_ra.png/40px-Old_Persian_ra.png 2x" data-file-width="193" data-file-height="194"></a> <a href="/wiki/File:Old_Persian_mi.png" class="image"><img alt="Old Persian mi.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Old_Persian_mi.png/24px-Old_Persian_mi.png" decoding="async" width="24" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Old_Persian_mi.png/36px-Old_Persian_mi.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Old_Persian_mi.png/48px-Old_Persian_mi.png 2x" data-file-width="220" data-file-height="184"></a> <a href="/wiki/File:Old_Persian_i.png" class="image"><img alt="Old Persian i.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Old_Persian_i.png/16px-Old_Persian_i.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Old_Persian_i.png/25px-Old_Persian_i.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Old_Persian_i.png/33px-Old_Persian_i.png 2x" data-file-width="156" data-file-height="190"></a> <a href="/wiki/File:Old_Persian_na.png" class="image"><img alt="Old Persian na.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Old_Persian_na.png/20px-Old_Persian_na.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Old_Persian_na.png/30px-Old_Persian_na.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Old_Persian_na.png/40px-Old_Persian_na.png 2x" data-file-width="184" data-file-height="184"></a>). The <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> terms <span lang="grc"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%BC%88%CF%81%CE%BC%CE%B5%CE%BD%CE%AF%CE%B1#Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="wikt:Ἀρμενία">Ἀρμενία</a></span> (<i>Armenía</i>) and <span lang="grc"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%BC%88%CF%81%CE%BC%CE%AD%CE%BD%CE%B9%CE%BF%CF%82#Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="wikt:Ἀρμένιος">Ἀρμένιοι</a></span> (<i>Arménioi</i>, "Armenians") are first mentioned by <a href="/wiki/Hecataeus_of_Miletus" title="Hecataeus of Miletus">Hecataeus of Miletus</a> (c. 550 BC – c. 476 BC).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Xenophon" title="Xenophon">Xenophon</a>, a Greek general serving in some of the Persian expeditions, describes many aspects of Armenian village life and hospitality in around 401 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some scholars have linked the name <i>Armenia</i> with the Early Bronze Age state of <i><a href="/wiki/Armani_(kingdom)" title="Armani (kingdom)">Armani (Armanum, Armi)</a></i> or the Late Bronze Age state of <i><a href="/wiki/Shupria" title="Shupria">Arme (Shupria)</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> These connections are inconclusive as it is not known what languages were spoken in these kingdoms. Additionally, while it is agreed that Arme was located to the immediate west of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Van" title="Lake Van">Lake Van</a> (and therefore in the greater Armenia region), the location of the older site of Armani is a matter of debate. Some modern researchers have placed it in the same general area of Arme, near modern <a href="/wiki/Samsat" title="Samsat">Samsat</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> and have suggested it was populated, at least partially, by an early Indo-European-speaking people.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> It has also been speculated that the land of <i>Ermenen</i> (located in or near <i><a href="/wiki/Mannaeans" title="Mannaeans">Minni</a></i>), mentioned by the Egyptian pharaoh <a href="/wiki/Thutmose_III" title="Thutmose III">Thutmose III</a> in 1446 BC, could be a reference to Armenia. </p>
      <p> According to the histories of both Moses of Chorene and Michael Chamchian, <i>Armenia</i> derives from the name of <a href="/wiki/Aram_(given_name)" title="Aram (given name)">Aram</a>, a lineal descendant of Hayk.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-battles_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-battles-41">[40]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Table_of_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Table of Nations">Table of Nations</a> lists <a href="/wiki/Aram,_son_of_Shem" title="Aram, son of Shem">Aram</a> as the son of <a href="/wiki/Shem" title="Shem">Shem</a>, to whom the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Jubilees" title="Book of Jubilees">Book of Jubilees</a> attests, </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>"And for Aram there came forth the fourth portion, all the land of Mesopotamia between the Tigris and the Euphrates to the north of the Chaldees to the border of the mountains of Asshur and the land of 'Arara.<sup id="cite_ref-pseudepigrapha_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pseudepigrapha-42">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-digitalcommons.andrews.edu_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-digitalcommons.andrews.edu-43">[42]</a></sup>"</p>
      </blockquote>
      <p> Jubilees 8:21 also apportions the Mountains of Ararat to <a href="/wiki/Shem" title="Shem">Shem</a>, which Jubilees 9:5 expounds to be apportioned to <a href="/wiki/Aram,_son_of_Shem" title="Aram, son of Shem">Aram</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pseudepigrapha_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pseudepigrapha-42">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-digitalcommons.andrews.edu_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-digitalcommons.andrews.edu-43">[42]</a></sup> The historian Flavius Josephus also states in his <a href="/wiki/Antiquities_of_the_Jews" title="Antiquities of the Jews">Antiquities of the Jews</a>, </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>"Aram had the Aramites, which the Greeks called <a href="/wiki/Syrians" title="Syrians">Syrians</a>;... Of the four sons of Aram, Uz founded <a href="/wiki/Trachonitis" class="mw-redirect" title="Trachonitis">Trachonitis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a>: this country lies between <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celesyria" class="mw-redirect" title="Celesyria">Celesyria</a>. Ul founded Armenia; and Gather the <a href="/wiki/Bactrians" class="mw-redirect" title="Bactrians">Bactrians</a>; and Mesa the Mesaneans; it is now called <a href="/wiki/Charax_Spasini" class="mw-redirect" title="Charax Spasini">Charax Spasini</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Armenia" title="History of Armenia">History of Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Armenia" title="Prehistoric Armenia">Prehistoric Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prehistory_of_the_Armenians" class="mw-redirect" title="Prehistory of the Armenians">Prehistory of the Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Satrapy_of_Armenia" title="Satrapy of Armenia">Satrapy of Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Armenia_(antiquity)" title="Kingdom of Armenia (antiquity)">Kingdom of Armenia (antiquity)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Armenia" title="Roman Armenia">Roman Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Armenia" title="Sasanian Armenia">Sasanian Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Armenia" title="Lesser Armenia">Lesser Armenia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_archeology" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian archeology">Armenian archeology</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:247px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Arshakuni_Armenia_150-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Arshakuni_Armenia_150-en.svg/245px-Arshakuni_Armenia_150-en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="245" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Arshakuni_Armenia_150-en.svg/368px-Arshakuni_Armenia_150-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Arshakuni_Armenia_150-en.svg/490px-Arshakuni_Armenia_150-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2717" data-file-height="1595"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Arshakuni_Armenia_150-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Historical Armenia, 150 BC
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Zorats_Karer_2008,_part_of_the_stone_circle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Zorats_Karer_2008%2C_part_of_the_stone_circle.jpg/220px-Zorats_Karer_2008%2C_part_of_the_stone_circle.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Zorats_Karer_2008%2C_part_of_the_stone_circle.jpg/330px-Zorats_Karer_2008%2C_part_of_the_stone_circle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Zorats_Karer_2008%2C_part_of_the_stone_circle.jpg/440px-Zorats_Karer_2008%2C_part_of_the_stone_circle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2176"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Zorats_Karer_2008,_part_of_the_stone_circle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bronze Age archeological site <a href="/wiki/Zorats_Karer" class="mw-redirect" title="Zorats Karer">Zorats Karer</a> (also known as <a href="/wiki/Zorats_Karer" class="mw-redirect" title="Zorats Karer">Karahunj</a>).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:247px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tigranes_four_Kings.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Tigranes_four_Kings.jpg/245px-Tigranes_four_Kings.jpg" decoding="async" width="245" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Tigranes_four_Kings.jpg/368px-Tigranes_four_Kings.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Tigranes_four_Kings.jpg/490px-Tigranes_four_Kings.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1856"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tigranes_four_Kings.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The King of Kings Tigranes the Great with four vassal Kings surrounding him
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenia lies in the highlands surrounding the mountains of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Ararat" title="Mount Ararat">Ararat</a>. There is evidence of an early civilisation in Armenia in the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> and earlier, dating to about 4000 BC. Archaeological surveys in 2010 and 2011 at the <a href="/wiki/Areni-1_cave_complex" class="mw-redirect" title="Areni-1 cave complex">Areni-1 cave complex</a> have resulted in the discovery of <a href="/wiki/Areni-1_shoe" title="Areni-1 shoe">the world's earliest known leather shoe</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CNNc_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNc-45">[44]</a></sup> skirt,<sup id="cite_ref-strawskirt_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strawskirt-46">[45]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Areni-1_winery" title="Areni-1 winery">wine-producing facility</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Geographic_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Geographic-47">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:112px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Xerxes_I_tomb_Armenian_soldier_circa_470_BCE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Xerxes_I_tomb_Armenian_soldier_circa_470_BCE.jpg/110px-Xerxes_I_tomb_Armenian_soldier_circa_470_BCE.jpg" decoding="async" width="110" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Xerxes_I_tomb_Armenian_soldier_circa_470_BCE.jpg/165px-Xerxes_I_tomb_Armenian_soldier_circa_470_BCE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Xerxes_I_tomb_Armenian_soldier_circa_470_BCE.jpg/220px-Xerxes_I_tomb_Armenian_soldier_circa_470_BCE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="1302"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Xerxes_I_tomb_Armenian_soldier_circa_470_BCE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Armenian soldier of the Achaemenid army, circa 470 BC. <a href="/wiki/Xerxes_I" title="Xerxes I">Xerxes I</a> tomb relief.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the story of <a href="/wiki/Hayk" title="Hayk">Hayk</a>, the legendary founder of Armenia, around 2107 BC Hayk fought against <a href="/wiki/Belus_(Babylonian)" title="Belus (Babylonian)">Belus</a>, the Babylonian God of War, at <a href="/wiki/%C3%87avu%C5%9Ftepe" title="Çavuştepe">Çavuştepe</a> along the Engil river to establish the very first Armenian state. Historically, this event coincides with the destruction of <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">Akkad</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Gutian_dynasty_of_Sumer" title="Gutian dynasty of Sumer">Gutian dynasty of Sumer</a> in 2115 BC,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> a time when Hayk may have left with the "more than 300 members of his household" as told in the legend, and also during the beginning of when a Mesopotamian Dark Age was occurring due to the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">Akkadian Empire</a> in 2154 BC which may have acted as a backdrop for the events in the legend making him leave Mesopotamia.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Several <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> cultures and states flourished in the area of Greater Armenia, including the <a href="/wiki/Trialeti_culture" title="Trialeti culture">Trialeti-Vanadzor culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hayasa-Azzi" title="Hayasa-Azzi">Hayasa-Azzi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mitanni" title="Mitanni">Mitanni</a> (located in southwestern historical Armenia), all of which are believed to have had Indo-European populations.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Nairi" title="Nairi">Nairi</a> confederation and its successor, <a href="/wiki/Urartu" title="Urartu">Urartu</a>, successively established their sovereignty over the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Highlands" title="Armenian Highlands">Armenian Highlands</a>. Each of the aforementioned nations and confederacies participated in the ethnogenesis of the <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> A large cuneiform lapidary inscription found in <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a> established that the modern capital of Armenia was founded in the summer of 782&nbsp;BC by King <a href="/wiki/Argishti_I_of_Urartu" title="Argishti I of Urartu">Argishti I</a>. Yerevan is the world's oldest city to have documented the exact date of its foundation. </p>
      <p>During the late 6th century BC, the <a href="/wiki/Satrapy_of_Armenia" title="Satrapy of Armenia">first geographical entity that was called Armenia</a> by neighbouring populations was established under the <a href="/wiki/Orontid_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Orontid Dynasty">Orontid Dynasty</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>, as part of the latters' territories. The kingdom became fully sovereign from the sphere of influence of the <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">Seleucid Empire</a> in 190 BC under King <a href="/wiki/Artaxias_I" title="Artaxias I">Artaxias I</a> and begun the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Artaxiad_dynasty" title="Artaxiad dynasty">Artaxiad dynasty</a>. Armenia reached its height between 95 and 66&nbsp;BC under <a href="/wiki/Tigranes_the_Great" title="Tigranes the Great">Tigranes the Great</a>, becoming the most powerful kingdom of its time east of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Garni_Temple_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Garni_Temple_02.JPG/220px-Garni_Temple_02.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Garni_Temple_02.JPG/330px-Garni_Temple_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Garni_Temple_02.JPG/440px-Garni_Temple_02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2462" data-file-height="2365"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Garni_Temple_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The pagan <a href="/wiki/Garni_Temple" class="mw-redirect" title="Garni Temple">Garni Temple</a>, probably built in the first century, is the only "Greco-Roman <a href="/wiki/Colonnade" title="Colonnade">colonnaded</a> building" in the <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">post-Soviet states</a><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:AMBS_by_Karl_von_Spruner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/AMBS_by_Karl_von_Spruner.jpg/220px-AMBS_by_Karl_von_Spruner.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/AMBS_by_Karl_von_Spruner.jpg/330px-AMBS_by_Karl_von_Spruner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/AMBS_by_Karl_von_Spruner.jpg/440px-AMBS_by_Karl_von_Spruner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1215"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:AMBS_by_Karl_von_Spruner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Armenia, Mesopotamia, Babylon and Assyria with adjacent regions. Karl von Spruner, published in 1865
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the next centuries, Armenia was in the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian Empire">Persian Empire</a>'s sphere of influence during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Tiridates_I_of_Armenia" title="Tiridates I of Armenia">Tiridates I</a>, the founder of the <a href="/wiki/Arsacid_dynasty_of_Armenia" title="Arsacid dynasty of Armenia">Arsacid dynasty of Armenia</a>, which itself was a branch of the <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian Empire</a>. Throughout its history, the kingdom of Armenia enjoyed both periods of independence and periods of autonomy subject to contemporary empires. Its strategic location between two continents has subjected it to invasions by many peoples, including <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyria</a> (under <a href="/wiki/Ashurbanipal" title="Ashurbanipal">Ashurbanipal</a>, at around 669–627 BC, the boundaries of Assyria reached as far as Armenia and the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Medes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanian Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_Empire" title="Seljuk Empire">Seljuk Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongols</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, the successive <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afsharid_dynasty" title="Afsharid dynasty">Afsharid</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajar</a> dynasties of Iran, and the Russians. </p>
      <p>Religion in ancient Armenia was historically related to a set of beliefs that, in Persia, led to the emergence of <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>. It particularly focused on the worship of <a href="/wiki/Mithra" title="Mithra">Mithra</a> and also included a pantheon of gods such as <a href="/wiki/Aramazd" title="Aramazd">Aramazd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vahagn" title="Vahagn">Vahagn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anahit" title="Anahit">Anahit</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Astghik" class="mw-redirect" title="Astghik">Astghik</a>. The country used the solar <a href="/wiki/Armenian_calendar" title="Armenian calendar">Armenian calendar</a>, which consisted of 12 months. </p>
      <p>Christianity spread into the country as early as AD 40. <a href="/wiki/Tiridates_III_of_Armenia" title="Tiridates III of Armenia">Tiridates III of Armenia</a> (238–314) made Christianity the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a> in 301,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-62">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-almanac_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-almanac-63">[62]</a></sup> partly, in defiance of the <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanian Empire</a>, it seems,<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-64">[63]</a></sup> becoming the first officially Christian state, ten years before the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> granted Christianity an official toleration under <a href="/wiki/Galerius" title="Galerius">Galerius</a>, and 36&nbsp;years before <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine the Great</a> was baptised. Prior to this, during the latter part of the Parthian period, Armenia was a predominantly Zoroastrian country.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-64">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the fall of the Kingdom of Armenia in 428, most of Armenia was incorporated as a <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Armenia" title="Sasanian Armenia"><i>marzpanate</i> within the Sasanian Empire</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Avarayr" title="Battle of Avarayr">Battle of Avarayr</a> in 451, Christian Armenians maintained their religion and Armenia gained autonomy. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span></h3> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">

          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">

      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Armenia" title="Medieval Armenia">Medieval Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Etchmiadzin_cathedral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Etchmiadzin_cathedral.jpg/220px-Etchmiadzin_cathedral.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Etchmiadzin_cathedral.jpg/330px-Etchmiadzin_cathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Etchmiadzin_cathedral.jpg/440px-Etchmiadzin_cathedral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1875"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Etchmiadzin_cathedral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Etchmiadzin_Cathedral" title="Etchmiadzin Cathedral">Etchmiadzin Cathedral</a>, Armenia's Mother Church traditionally dated 303 AD, is considered the oldest cathedral in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Armenia" title="Sasanian Armenia">Sasanian period</a> (428–636), Armenia emerged as <a href="/wiki/Arminiya" title="Arminiya">Arminiya</a>, an autonomous principality under the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a>, reuniting Armenian lands previously taken by the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> as well. The principality was ruled by the Prince of Armenia, and recognised by the <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Caliph</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Byzantine_emperors" title="List of Byzantine emperors">Byzantine Emperor</a>. It was part of the administrative division/emirate <i><a href="/wiki/Arminiya" title="Arminiya">Arminiya</a></i> created by the Arabs, which also included parts of Georgia and <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Albania" title="Caucasian Albania">Caucasian Albania</a>, and had its centre in the Armenian city, <a href="/wiki/Dvin_(ancient_city)" title="Dvin (ancient city)">Dvin</a>. Arminiya lasted until 884, when it regained its independence from the weakened <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid Caliphate</a> under <a href="/wiki/Ashot_I_of_Armenia" title="Ashot I of Armenia">Ashot I of Armenia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECanardCahen1960_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECanardCahen1960-68">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The reemergent Armenian kingdom was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Bagratuni_dynasty" title="Bagratuni dynasty">Bagratuni dynasty</a> and lasted until 1045. In time, several areas of the Bagratid Armenia separated as independent kingdoms and principalities such as the Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Vaspurakan" title="Vaspurakan">Vaspurakan</a> ruled by the House of <a href="/wiki/Artsruni" class="mw-redirect" title="Artsruni">Artsruni</a> in the south, Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Syunik_Province" title="Syunik Province">Syunik</a> in the east, or <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Artsakh" title="Kingdom of Artsakh">Kingdom of Artsakh</a> on the territory of modern <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a>, while still recognising the supremacy of the Bagratid kings. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cilician_Armenia-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Cilician_Armenia-en.svg/220px-Cilician_Armenia-en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Cilician_Armenia-en.svg/330px-Cilician_Armenia-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Cilician_Armenia-en.svg/440px-Cilician_Armenia-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2508" data-file-height="1789"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cilician_Armenia-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Kingdom_of_Cilicia" title="Armenian Kingdom of Cilicia">Armenian Kingdom of Cilicia</a>, 1198–1375.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1045, the Byzantine Empire conquered Bagratid Armenia. Soon, the other Armenian states fell under Byzantine control as well. The Byzantine rule was short lived, as in 1071 the <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_Empire" title="Seljuk Empire">Seljuk Empire</a> defeated the Byzantines and conquered Armenia at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manzikert" title="Battle of Manzikert">Battle of Manzikert</a>, establishing the Seljuk Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> To escape death or servitude at the hands of those who had assassinated his relative, <a href="/wiki/Gagik_II_of_Armenia" title="Gagik II of Armenia">Gagik II of Armenia</a>, King of <a href="/wiki/Ani" title="Ani">Ani</a>, an Armenian named <a href="/wiki/Ruben_I,_Prince_of_Armenia" title="Ruben I, Prince of Armenia">Ruben I, Prince of Armenia</a>, went with some of his countrymen into the gorges of the <a href="/wiki/Taurus_Mountains" title="Taurus Mountains">Taurus Mountains</a> and then into <a href="/wiki/Tarsus,_Mersin" title="Tarsus, Mersin">Tarsus</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cilicia" title="Cilicia">Cilicia</a>. The Byzantine governor of the palace gave them shelter where the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Kingdom_of_Cilicia" title="Armenian Kingdom of Cilicia">Armenian Kingdom of Cilicia</a> was eventually established on 6 January 1198 under <a href="/wiki/Leo_I,_King_of_Armenia" title="Leo I, King of Armenia">Leo I, King of Armenia</a>, a descendant of Prince Ruben. </p>
      <p>Cilicia was a strong ally of the <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">European Crusaders</a>, and saw itself as a bastion of <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a> in the East. Cilicia's significance in Armenian history and statehood is also attested by the transfer of the seat of the Catholicos of the Armenian Apostolic Church, the spiritual leader of the Armenian people, to the region. </p>
      <p>The Seljuk Empire soon started to collapse. In the early 12th century, Armenian princes of the Zakarid family drove out the Seljuk Turks and established a semi-independent principality in northern and eastern Armenia known as <a href="/wiki/Zakarid_Armenia" title="Zakarid Armenia">Zakarid Armenia</a>, which lasted under the patronage of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Georgia_(country)" title="History of Georgia (country)">Georgian Kingdom</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Orbelian_Dynasty" title="Orbelian Dynasty">Orbelian Dynasty</a> shared control with the Zakarids in various parts of the country, especially in Syunik and <a href="/wiki/Vayots_Dzor_Province" title="Vayots Dzor Province">Vayots Dzor</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hasan-Jalalyan" title="House of Hasan-Jalalyan">House of Hasan-Jalalyan</a> controlled provinces of <a href="/wiki/Artsakh_(historic_province)" title="Artsakh (historic province)">Artsakh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Utik" title="Utik">Utik</a> as the Kingdom of Artsakh. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Modern_era">Early Modern era</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Armenia_(1502%E2%80%931828)" title="Iranian Armenia (1502–1828)">Iranian Armenia (1502–1828)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Armenians in the Ottoman Empire">Armenians in the Ottoman Empire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Armenia" title="Russian Armenia">Russian Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_Safavid_persia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Map_Safavid_persia.png/220px-Map_Safavid_persia.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Map_Safavid_persia.png/330px-Map_Safavid_persia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Map_Safavid_persia.png/440px-Map_Safavid_persia.png 2x" data-file-width="1033" data-file-height="717"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Map_Safavid_persia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>In 1501–02, most of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Armenia" title="Eastern Armenia">Eastern Armenian</a> territories including Yerevan were conquered by the emerging <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid dynasty</a> of Iran led by Shah <a href="/wiki/Ismail_I" title="Ismail I">Ismail I</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the 1230s, the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> conquered Zakarid Armenia and then the remainder of Armenia. The Mongolian invasions were soon followed by those of other Central Asian tribes, such as the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Koyunlu" class="mw-redirect" title="Kara Koyunlu">Kara Koyunlu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timurid_dynasty" title="Timurid dynasty">Timurid dynasty</a> and <a href="/wiki/A%C4%9F_Qoyunlu" class="mw-redirect" title="Ağ Qoyunlu">Ağ Qoyunlu</a>, which continued from the 13th century until the 15th century. After incessant invasions, each bringing destruction to the country, with time Armenia became weakened. </p>
      <p>In the 16th century, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid dynasty</a> of Iran divided Armenia. From the early 16th century, both <a href="/wiki/Western_Armenia" title="Western Armenia">Western Armenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Armenia" title="Eastern Armenia">Eastern Armenia</a> fell to the Safavid Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ward2014_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ward2014-71">[70]</a></sup> Owing to the century long <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Safavid_relations" title="Ottoman–Safavid relations">Turco-Iranian geopolitical rivalry</a> that would last in Western Asia, significant parts of the region were frequently fought over between the two rivalling empires during the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Persian_Wars" title="Ottoman–Persian Wars">Ottoman–Persian Wars</a>. From the mid 16th century with the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Amasya" title="Peace of Amasya">Peace of Amasya</a>, and decisively from the first half of the 17th century with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Zuhab" title="Treaty of Zuhab">Treaty of Zuhab</a> until the first half of the 19th century,<sup id="cite_ref-HerzigKurkchiyan2004_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HerzigKurkchiyan2004-72">[71]</a></sup> Eastern Armenia was ruled by the successive Safavid, <a href="/wiki/Afsharid_dynasty" title="Afsharid dynasty">Afsharid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajar</a> empires, while Western Armenia remained under <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Turkey">Ottoman</a> rule. </p>
      <p>From 1604, <a href="/wiki/Abbas_I_of_Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Abbas I of Persia">Abbas I of Iran</a> implemented a "<a href="/wiki/Scorched_earth" title="Scorched earth">scorched earth</a>" policy in the region to protect his north-western frontier against any <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Safavid_War_(1603%E2%80%931618)" title="Ottoman–Safavid War (1603–1618)">invading Ottoman forces</a>, a policy that involved a <a href="/wiki/History_of_Armenia#Persian_Armenia" title="History of Armenia">forced resettlement</a> of masses of Armenians outside of their homelands.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Capture_of_Erivan_Fortress_by_Russia,_1827_(by_Franz_Roubaud).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Capture_of_Erivan_Fortress_by_Russia%2C_1827_%28by_Franz_Roubaud%29.jpg/220px-Capture_of_Erivan_Fortress_by_Russia%2C_1827_%28by_Franz_Roubaud%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Capture_of_Erivan_Fortress_by_Russia%2C_1827_%28by_Franz_Roubaud%29.jpg/330px-Capture_of_Erivan_Fortress_by_Russia%2C_1827_%28by_Franz_Roubaud%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Capture_of_Erivan_Fortress_by_Russia%2C_1827_%28by_Franz_Roubaud%29.jpg/440px-Capture_of_Erivan_Fortress_by_Russia%2C_1827_%28by_Franz_Roubaud%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1159" data-file-height="851"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Capture_of_Erivan_Fortress_by_Russia,_1827_(by_Franz_Roubaud).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Erivan" title="Capture of Erivan">Capture of Erivan</a> fortress by Russian troops in 1827 during the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1826%E2%80%9328)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Persian War (1826–28)">Russo-Persian War (1826–28)</a> by <a href="/wiki/Franz_Roubaud" title="Franz Roubaud">Franz Roubaud</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 1813 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Gulistan" title="Treaty of Gulistan">Treaty of Gulistan</a> and the 1828 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Turkmenchay" title="Treaty of Turkmenchay">Treaty of Turkmenchay</a>, following the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1804%E2%80%9313)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Persian War (1804–13)">Russo-Persian War (1804–13)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1826%E2%80%9328)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Persian War (1826–28)">Russo-Persian War (1826–28)</a>, respectively, the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajar dynasty</a> of Iran was forced to irrevocably cede <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Armenia" title="Eastern Armenia">Eastern Armenia</a>, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Erivan_Khanate" title="Erivan Khanate">Erivan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karabakh_Khanate" title="Karabakh Khanate">Karabakh Khanates</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Russia">Imperial Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mikaberidze2011_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mikaberidze2011-74">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dowling2014_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dowling2014-75">[74]</a></sup> This period is known as <a href="/wiki/Russian_Armenia" title="Russian Armenia">Russian Armenia</a>. </p>
      <p>While Western Armenia still remained under Ottoman rule, the Armenians were granted considerable autonomy within their own <a href="/wiki/Enclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Enclave">enclaves</a> and lived in relative harmony with other groups in the empire (including the ruling Turks). However, as Christians under a strict Muslim <a href="/wiki/Social_structure" title="Social structure">social structure</a>, Armenians faced pervasive discrimination. When they began pushing for more rights within the Ottoman Empire, Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Hamid_II" title="Abdul Hamid II">Abdul Hamid II</a>, in response, organised state-sponsored massacres against the Armenians between 1894 and 1896, resulting in an estimated death toll of 80,000 to 300,000 people. The <a href="/wiki/Hamidian_massacres" title="Hamidian massacres">Hamidian massacres</a>, as they came to be known, gave Hamid international infamy as the "Red Sultan" or "Bloody Sultan".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 1890s, the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Revolutionary_Federation" title="Armenian Revolutionary Federation">Armenian Revolutionary Federation</a>, commonly known as <i>Dashnaktsutyun</i>, became active within the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> with the aim of unifying the various small groups in the empire that were advocating for reform and defending Armenian villages from massacres that were widespread in some of the Armenian-populated areas of the empire. Dashnaktsutyun members also formed <a href="/wiki/Armenian_fedayi" title="Armenian fedayi">Armenian fedayi</a> groups that defended Armenian civilians through armed resistance. The Dashnaks also worked for the wider goal of creating a "free, independent and unified" Armenia, although they sometimes set aside this goal in favour of a more realistic approach, such as advocating autonomy. </p>
      <p>The Ottoman Empire began to collapse, and in 1908, the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution" title="Young Turk Revolution">Young Turk Revolution</a> overthrew the government of Sultan Hamid. In April 1909, the <a href="/wiki/Adana_massacre" title="Adana massacre">Adana massacre</a> occurred in the <a href="/wiki/Adana_Vilayet" title="Adana Vilayet">Adana Vilayet</a> of the Ottoman Empire resulting in the deaths of as many as 20,000–30,000 Armenians. The Armenians living in the empire hoped that the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress" title="Committee of Union and Progress">Committee of Union and Progress</a> would change their second-class status. The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_reform_package" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian reform package">Armenian reform package</a> (1914) was presented as a solution by appointing an <a href="/wiki/Inspector_general" title="Inspector general">inspector general</a> over Armenian issues.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I_and_the_Armenian_Genocide">World War I and the Armenian Genocide</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian Genocide</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ambassador_Morgenthau%27s_Story_p314.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Ambassador_Morgenthau%27s_Story_p314.jpg/220px-Ambassador_Morgenthau%27s_Story_p314.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Ambassador_Morgenthau%27s_Story_p314.jpg/330px-Ambassador_Morgenthau%27s_Story_p314.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Ambassador_Morgenthau%27s_Story_p314.jpg/440px-Ambassador_Morgenthau%27s_Story_p314.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3999" data-file-height="2731"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Morgenthau336.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian Genocide</a> victims in 1915.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The outbreak of World War I led to confrontation between the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Caucasus Campaign">Caucasus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persian_Campaign" title="Persian Campaign">Persian Campaigns</a>. The new government in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> began to look on the Armenians with distrust and suspicion, because the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russian_Army" title="Imperial Russian Army">Imperial Russian Army</a> contained a contingent of <a href="/wiki/Armenian_volunteer_units" title="Armenian volunteer units">Armenian volunteers</a>. On 24 April 1915, <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_Armenian_intellectuals_on_24_April_1915" title="Deportation of Armenian intellectuals on 24 April 1915">Armenian intellectuals were arrested by Ottoman authorities</a> and, with the <a href="/wiki/Tehcir_Law" title="Tehcir Law">Tehcir Law</a> (29 May 1915), eventually a large proportion of Armenians living in <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> perished in what has become known as the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian Genocide</a>. </p>
      <p>The genocide was implemented in two phases: the wholesale killing of the able-bodied male population through massacre and subjection of army conscripts to forced labour, followed by the deportation of women, children, the elderly and infirm on <a href="/wiki/Death_march" title="Death march">death marches</a> leading to the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian desert">Syrian desert</a>. Driven forward by military escorts, the deportees were deprived of food and water and subjected to periodic robbery, rape, and massacre.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> There was local <a href="/wiki/Armenian_resistance_during_the_Armenian_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian resistance during the Armenian Genocide">Armenian resistance</a> in the region, developed against the activities of the Ottoman Empire. The events of 1915 to 1917 are regarded by Armenians and the vast majority of Western historians to have been state-sponsored mass killings, or genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Turkish authorities deny the genocide took place to this day. The Armenian Genocide is acknowledged to have been one of the first modern <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocides</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24.04.1998_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24.04.1998-81">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-82">[81]</a></sup> According to the research conducted by <a href="/wiki/Arnold_J._Toynbee" title="Arnold J. Toynbee">Arnold J. Toynbee</a>, an estimated 600,000 Armenians died during deportation from 1915 to 1916. This figure, however, accounts for solely the first year of the Genocide and does not take into account those who died or were killed after the report was compiled on 24 May 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Genocide_Scholars" title="International Association of Genocide Scholars">International Association of Genocide Scholars</a> places the death toll at "more than a million".<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> The total number of people killed has been most widely estimated at between 1 and 1.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Armenia and the Armenian diaspora have been campaigning for <a href="/wiki/Recognition_of_the_Armenian_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Recognition of the Armenian Genocide">official recognition</a> of the events as genocide for over 30&nbsp;years. These events are traditionally commemorated yearly on 24 April, the Armenian Martyr Day, or the Day of the Armenian Genocide.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Republic_of_Armenia">First Republic of Armenia</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Armenia" title="First Republic of Armenia">First Republic of Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:First_Republic_of_Armenia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/First_Republic_of_Armenia.png/220px-First_Republic_of_Armenia.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/First_Republic_of_Armenia.png/330px-First_Republic_of_Armenia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/First_Republic_of_Armenia.png/440px-First_Republic_of_Armenia.png 2x" data-file-width="1306" data-file-height="855"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:First_Republic_of_Armenia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FF7F00; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Territory held by <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Armenia" title="First Republic of Armenia">Armenia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Karabakh_Council" title="Karabakh Council">Karabakh Council</a> at some point
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:beige; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Area given to Armenia by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres" title="Treaty of Sèvres">Treaty of Sèvres</a>, which was never entered into force.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Yerevan_Hanrapetutyan_street_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Yerevan_Hanrapetutyan_street_02.jpg/220px-Yerevan_Hanrapetutyan_street_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Yerevan_Hanrapetutyan_street_02.jpg/330px-Yerevan_Hanrapetutyan_street_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Yerevan_Hanrapetutyan_street_02.jpg/440px-Yerevan_Hanrapetutyan_street_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Yerevan_Hanrapetutyan_street_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Government house of the <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Armenia" title="First Republic of Armenia">First Republic of Armenia</a> (1918–1920).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Caucasus_Army_(World_War_I)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Caucasus Army (World War I)">Russian Caucasus Army</a> of Imperial forces commanded by <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Yudenich" title="Nikolai Yudenich">Nikolai Yudenich</a> and Armenians in volunteer units and Armenian militia led by <a href="/wiki/Andranik_Ozanian" class="mw-redirect" title="Andranik Ozanian">Andranik Ozanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tovmas_Nazarbekian" title="Tovmas Nazarbekian">Tovmas Nazarbekian</a> succeeded in gaining most of Ottoman Armenia during World War I, their gains were lost with the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">Bolshevik Revolution of 1917</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> At the time, Russian-controlled <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Armenia" title="Eastern Armenia">Eastern Armenia</a>, Georgia, and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> attempted to bond together in the <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasian_Democratic_Federative_Republic" title="Transcaucasian Democratic Federative Republic">Transcaucasian Democratic Federative Republic</a>. This federation, however, lasted from only February to May 1918, when all three parties decided to dissolve it. As a result, the Dashnaktsutyun government of Eastern Armenia declared its independence on 28 May as the <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Armenia" title="First Republic of Armenia">First Republic of Armenia</a> under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Aram_Manukian" title="Aram Manukian">Aram Manukian</a>. </p>
      <p>The First Republic's short-lived independence was fraught with war, <a href="/wiki/Territorial_dispute" title="Territorial dispute">territorial disputes</a>, and a mass influx of refugees from Ottoman Armenia, bringing with them disease and starvation. The <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Entente Powers</a> sought to help the newly founded Armenian state through relief funds and other forms of support. </p>
      <p>At the end of the war, the victorious powers sought to divide up the Ottoman Empire. Signed between the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied and Associated Powers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> at <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A8vres" title="Sèvres">Sèvres</a> on 10 August 1920, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres" title="Treaty of Sèvres">Treaty of Sèvres</a> promised to maintain the existence of the Armenian republic and to attach the former territories of Ottoman Armenia to it. Because the new borders of Armenia were to be drawn by United States President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a>, Ottoman Armenia was also referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Wilsonian_Armenia" title="Wilsonian Armenia">Wilsonian Armenia</a>". In addition, just days prior, on 5 August 1920, <a href="/wiki/Mihran_Damadian" title="Mihran Damadian">Mihran Damadian</a> of the Armenian National Union, the de facto Armenian administration in Cilicia, declared the independence of <a href="/wiki/Cilicia" title="Cilicia">Cilicia</a> as an Armenian autonomous republic under French protectorate.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There was even consideration of making Armenia a mandate under the protection of the United States. The treaty, however, was rejected by the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_National_Movement" title="Turkish National Movement">Turkish National Movement</a>, and never came into effect. The movement used the treaty as the occasion to declare itself the rightful <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Turkey" title="Politics of Turkey">government of Turkey</a>, replacing the monarchy based in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> with a republic based in <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:11thRedArmyYerevan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/11thRedArmyYerevan.jpg/220px-11thRedArmyYerevan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/11thRedArmyYerevan.jpg/330px-11thRedArmyYerevan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/11thRedArmyYerevan.jpg/440px-11thRedArmyYerevan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1768" data-file-height="1302"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:11thRedArmyYerevan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Advance of the <a href="/wiki/11th_Army_(RSFSR)" title="11th Army (RSFSR)">11th Red Army</a> into the city of Yerevan.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1920, Turkish nationalist forces invaded the fledgling Armenian republic from the east. Turkish forces under the command of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A2z%C4%B1m_Karabekir" title="Kâzım Karabekir">Kazım Karabekir</a> captured Armenian territories that Russia had annexed in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%9378)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877–78)">1877–1878 Russo-Turkish War</a> and occupied the old city of Alexandropol (present-day <a href="/wiki/Gyumri" title="Gyumri">Gyumri</a>). The violent conflict finally concluded with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Alexandropol" title="Treaty of Alexandropol">Treaty of Alexandropol</a> on 2 December 1920. The treaty forced Armenia to disarm most of its <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed forces">military forces</a>, cede all former Ottoman territory granted to it by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres" title="Treaty of Sèvres">Treaty of Sèvres</a>, and to give up all the "Wilsonian Armenia" granted to it at the Sèvres treaty. Simultaneously, the <a href="/wiki/11th_Army_(RSFSR)" title="11th Army (RSFSR)">Soviet Eleventh Army</a>, under the command of <a href="/wiki/Grigoriy_Ordzhonikidze" class="mw-redirect" title="Grigoriy Ordzhonikidze">Grigoriy Ordzhonikidze</a>, invaded Armenia at Karavansarai (present-day <a href="/wiki/Ijevan" title="Ijevan">Ijevan</a>) on 29 November. By 4 December, Ordzhonikidze's forces entered Yerevan and the short-lived Armenian republic collapsed. </p>
      <p>After the fall of the republic, the <a href="/wiki/February_Uprising" title="February Uprising">February Uprising</a> soon took place in 1921, and led to the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Mountainous_Armenia" title="Republic of Mountainous Armenia">Republic of Mountainous Armenia</a> by Armenian forces under command of <a href="/wiki/Garegin_Nzhdeh" title="Garegin Nzhdeh">Garegin Nzhdeh</a> on 26 April, which fought off both Soviet and Turkish intrusions in the Zangezur region of southern Armenia. After Soviet agreements to include the <a href="/wiki/Syunik_Province" title="Syunik Province">Syunik Province</a> in Armenia's borders, the rebellion ended and the Red Army took control of the region on 13 July. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armenian_SSR">Armenian SSR</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic">Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_the_Armenian_SSR.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Emblem_of_the_Armenian_SSR.svg/220px-Emblem_of_the_Armenian_SSR.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Emblem_of_the_Armenian_SSR.svg/330px-Emblem_of_the_Armenian_SSR.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Emblem_of_the_Armenian_SSR.svg/440px-Emblem_of_the_Armenian_SSR.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="605" data-file-height="604"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_the_Armenian_SSR.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The coat of arms of <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic">Soviet Armenia</a> depicting <a href="/wiki/Mount_Ararat" title="Mount Ararat">Mount Ararat</a> in the centre.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenia was annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> and along with <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Georgia" title="Democratic Republic of Georgia">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan</a>, was incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Soviet_Socialist_Republics" class="mw-redirect" title="Union of Soviet Socialist Republics">Union of Soviet Socialist Republics</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasian_SFSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Transcaucasian SFSR">Transcaucasian SFSR</a> (TSFSR) on 4 March 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-main1_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-main1-88">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BSE_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSE-89">[88]</a></sup> With this annexation, the Treaty of Alexandropol was superseded by the Turkish-Soviet <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kars" title="Treaty of Kars">Treaty of Kars</a>. In the agreement, Turkey allowed the Soviet Union to assume control over <a href="/wiki/Adjara" title="Adjara">Adjara</a> with the port city of <a href="/wiki/Batumi" title="Batumi">Batumi</a> in return for sovereignty over the cities of <a href="/wiki/Kars" title="Kars">Kars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ardahan" title="Ardahan">Ardahan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/I%C4%9Fd%C4%B1r" title="Iğdır">Iğdır</a>, all of which were part of Russian Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-main1_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-main1-88">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BSE_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSE-89">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The TSFSR existed from 1922 to 1936, when it was divided up into three separate entities (<a href="/wiki/Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic">Armenian SSR</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic">Azerbaijan SSR</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic">Georgian SSR</a>). Armenians enjoyed a period of relative stability within USSR. They received medicine, food, and other provisions from Moscow, and communist rule proved to be a soothing balm in contrast to the turbulent final years of the Ottoman Empire. The situation was difficult for the church, which struggled with <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_soviet_union" class="mw-redirect" title="Religion in soviet union">secular policies of USSR</a>. After the death of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> and events occurred during <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> became the general secretary of the <a href="/wiki/CPSU" class="mw-redirect" title="CPSU">CPSU</a>, the most powerful position in the USSR of the time.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> </p>
