      <p>Armenia was not the scene of any battles in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">World War II</a>. An estimated 500,000 Armenians (nearly a third of the population) served in the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> during the war, and 175,000 died.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It is claimed that the freedom index in the region had seen an improvement after the <a href="/wiki/State_funeral_of_Joseph_Stalin" class="mw-redirect" title="State funeral of Joseph Stalin">death of Joseph Stalin</a> in 1953 the and emergence of <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> as the new general secretary of the <a href="/wiki/CPSU" class="mw-redirect" title="CPSU">CPSU</a>. Soon, life in Armenia's SSR began to see rapid improvement. The church, which was limited during the secretaryship of Stalin, was revived when <a href="/wiki/Catholicos_of_All_Armenians" title="Catholicos of All Armenians">Catholicos</a> <a href="/wiki/Vazgen_I" title="Vazgen I">Vazgen I</a> assumed the duties of his office in 1955. In 1967, a memorial to the victims of the Armenian Genocide was built at the <a href="/wiki/Tsitsernakaberd" title="Tsitsernakaberd">Tsitsernakaberd</a> hill above the <a href="/wiki/Hrazdan" title="Hrazdan">Hrazdan</a> <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">gorge</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a>. This occurred after <a href="/wiki/1965_Yerevan_demonstrations" title="1965 Yerevan demonstrations">mass demonstrations</a> took place on the tragic event's fiftieth anniversary in 1965. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Karabakh_movement_demonstration_at_Yerevan_Opera_square_(4).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Karabakh_movement_demonstration_at_Yerevan_Opera_square_%284%29.jpg/220px-Karabakh_movement_demonstration_at_Yerevan_Opera_square_%284%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Karabakh_movement_demonstration_at_Yerevan_Opera_square_%284%29.jpg/330px-Karabakh_movement_demonstration_at_Yerevan_Opera_square_%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Karabakh_movement_demonstration_at_Yerevan_Opera_square_%284%29.jpg/440px-Karabakh_movement_demonstration_at_Yerevan_Opera_square_%284%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="849" data-file-height="518"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Karabakh_movement_demonstration_at_Yerevan_Opera_square_(4).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Armenians gather at <a href="/wiki/Freedom_Square,_Yerevan" title="Freedom Square, Yerevan">Theater Square</a> in central <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a> to claim unification of <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast">Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian SSR">Armenian SSR</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Gorbachev</a> era of the 1980s, with the reforms of <a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">Glasnost</a> and <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">Perestroika</a>, Armenians began to demand better environmental care for their country, opposing the pollution that Soviet-built factories brought. Tensions also developed between Soviet Azerbaijan and its autonomous district of <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a>, a majority-Armenian region. About 484,000 <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Azerbaijan" title="Armenians in Azerbaijan">Armenians</a> lived in Azerbaijan in 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> The Armenians of Karabakh demanded unification with Soviet Armenia. Peaceful protests in Armenia supporting the Karabakh Armenians were met with anti-Armenian <a href="/wiki/Pogrom" title="Pogrom">pogroms</a> in Azerbaijan, such as the one in <a href="/wiki/Sumgait_pogrom" title="Sumgait pogrom">Sumgait</a>, which was followed by <a href="/wiki/Gugark_massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Gugark massacre">anti-Azerbaijani violence</a> in Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> Compounding Armenia's problems was a <a href="/wiki/1988_Armenian_earthquake" title="1988 Armenian earthquake">devastating earthquake</a> in 1988 with a <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">moment magnitude</a> of 7.2.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Gorbachev's inability to alleviate any of Armenia's problems created disillusionment among the Armenians and fed a growing hunger for independence. In May 1990, the New <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Army">Armenian Army</a> (NAA) was established, serving as a defence force separate from the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>. Clashes soon broke out between the NAA and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Ministry_of_Internal_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Ministry of Internal Affairs">Soviet Internal Security Forces</a> (MVD) troops based in Yerevan when Armenians decided to commemorate the establishment of the 1918 First Republic of Armenia. The violence resulted in the deaths of five Armenians killed in a shootout with the MVD at the railway station. Witnesses there claimed that the MVD used excessive force and that they had instigated the fighting. </p>
      <p>Further firefights between Armenian militiamen and Soviet troops occurred in <a href="/wiki/Nubarashen" class="mw-redirect" title="Nubarashen">Sovetashen</a>, near the capital and resulted in the deaths of over 26 people, mostly Armenians. The <a href="/wiki/Pogrom_of_Armenians_in_Baku" class="mw-redirect" title="Pogrom of Armenians in Baku">pogrom of Armenians in Baku</a> in January 1990 forced almost all of the 200,000 Armenians in the Azerbaijani capital <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> to flee to Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> On 23 August 1990, Armenia declared its sovereignty on its territory. On 17 March 1991, Armenia, along with the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a>, Georgia and <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldova</a>, boycotted a nationwide <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_Union_referendum" title="1991 Soviet Union referendum">referendum</a> in which 78% of all voters voted for the retention of the Soviet Union in a reformed form.<sup id="cite_ref-NewsBrief_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewsBrief-96">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restoration_of_independence">Restoration of independence</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Armenia#Independent_Armenia_(1991-today)" title="History of Armenia">History of Armenia §&nbsp;Independent Armenia (1991-today)</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:NKR_war.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NKR_war.JPG/220px-NKR_war.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NKR_war.JPG/330px-NKR_war.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NKR_war.JPG/440px-NKR_war.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1818" data-file-height="1228"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:NKR_war.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Armenian soldiers in 2008, during the ongoing and unresolved <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_conflict" title="Nagorno-Karabakh conflict">Nagorno-Karabakh conflict</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 21 September 1991, Armenia officially declared its <a href="/wiki/Statehood" class="mw-redirect" title="Statehood">statehood</a> after the <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt">failed August coup</a> in Moscow, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">RSFSR</a>. <a href="/wiki/Levon_Ter-Petrosyan" title="Levon Ter-Petrosyan">Levon Ter-Petrosyan</a> was popularly elected the first President of the newly independent Republic of Armenia on 16 October 1991. He had risen to prominence by leading the <a href="/wiki/Karabakh_movement" title="Karabakh movement">Karabakh movement</a> for the unification of the Armenian-populated <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Croissant_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Croissant-97">[96]</a></sup> On 26 December 1991, the Soviet Union ceased to exist and Armenia's independence was recognised. </p>
      <p>Ter-Petrosyan led Armenia alongside Defense Minister <a href="/wiki/Vazgen_Sargsyan" title="Vazgen Sargsyan">Vazgen Sargsyan</a> through the <a href="/wiki/First_Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="First Nagorno-Karabakh War">First Nagorno-Karabakh War</a> with neighbouring Azerbaijan. The initial post-Soviet years were marred by economic difficulties, which had their roots early in the Karabakh conflict when the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_Popular_Front_Party" title="Azerbaijani Popular Front Party">Azerbaijani Popular Front</a> managed to pressure the Azerbaijan SSR to instigate a railway and air <a href="/wiki/Blockade" title="Blockade">blockade</a> against Armenia. This move effectively crippled Armenia's economy as 85% of its cargo and goods arrived through rail traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-Croissant_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Croissant-97">[96]</a></sup> In 1993, Turkey joined the blockade against Armenia in support of Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-GHF_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GHF-98">[97]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:September_21,_2011_parade,_Yerevan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg/170px-September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg/255px-September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg/340px-September_21%2C_2011_parade%2C_Yerevan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:September_21,_2011_parade,_Yerevan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>21 September 2011 parade in Yerevan, marking the 20th anniversary of Armenia's re-independence.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Karabakh war ended after a Russian-brokered <a href="/wiki/Ceasefire" title="Ceasefire">cease-fire</a> was put in place in 1994. The war was a success for the Karabakh Armenian forces who managed to capture 16% of Azerbaijan's internationally recognised territory including Nagorno-Karabakh itself.<sup id="cite_ref-DeWaal_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeWaal-99">[98]</a></sup> The Armenian backed forces remained in control of practically all of that territory until 2020. The economies of both Armenia and Azerbaijan have been hurt in the absence of a complete resolution and Armenia's borders with Turkey and Azerbaijan remain closed. By the time both Azerbaijan and Armenia had finally agreed to a ceasefire in 1994, an estimated 30,000 people had been killed and over a million had been displaced.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> Several thousand were killed in the later 2020 Karabakh war. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern-day_Armenia">Modern-day Armenia</span></h3> 
      <p>In the 21st century Armenia faces many hardships. It has made a full switch to a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>. One study ranks it the 41st most "economically free" nation in the world, as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-economic-index_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economic-index-101">[100]</a></sup> Its relations with Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> have allowed Armenia to increase trade.<sup id="cite_ref-EPP_Group_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPP_Group-102">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Arka_news_agency_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arka_news_agency-103">[102]</a></sup> Gas, oil, and other supplies come through two vital routes: Iran and Georgia. As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Armenia maintained cordial relations with both countries.<sup id="cite_ref-European_Dialogue_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_Dialogue-104">[103]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated. (January 2020)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2018_Armenian_revolution" title="2018 Armenian revolution">2018 Armenian Revolution</a> was a series of anti-government protests in Armenia from April to May 2018 staged by various political and civil groups led by a member of the Armenian parliament — <a href="/wiki/Nikol_Pashinyan" title="Nikol Pashinyan">Nikol Pashinyan</a> (head of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Contract_(Armenia)" title="Civil Contract (Armenia)">Civil Contract</a> party). Protests and marches took place initially in response to <a href="/wiki/Serzh_Sargsyan" title="Serzh Sargsyan">Serzh Sargsyan's</a> third consecutive term as President of Armenia and later against the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_of_Armenia" title="Republican Party of Armenia">Republican Party</a> controlled government in general. Pashinyan declared it<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2021)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> a "<a href="/wiki/Velvet_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Velvet revolution">velvet revolution</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2018, Armenian parliament elected <a href="/wiki/Armen_Sarksyan" title="Armen Sarksyan">Armen Sarksyan</a> as the new President of Armenia. The controversial constitutional reform to reduce presidential power was implemented, while the authority of the prime minister was strengthened.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> In May 2018, parliament elected opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Nikol_Pashinyan" title="Nikol Pashinyan">Nikol Pashinyan</a> as the new prime minister. His predecessor Serzh Sargsyan resigned two weeks earlier following widespread anti-government demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 27 September 2020, a full-scale war erupted due to the unresolved <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_conflict" title="Nagorno-Karabakh conflict">Nagorno-Karabakh conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> Both the armed forces of Armenia and Azerbaijan reported military and civilian casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_ceasefire_agreement" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh ceasefire agreement">Nagorno-Karabakh ceasefire agreement</a> to end the six-week <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_war" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh war">war between Armenia and Azerbaijan</a> was seen by many as Armenia's defeat and capitulation.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Armenia" title="Geography of Armenia">Geography of Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenia is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Geopolitical" class="mw-redirect" title="Geopolitical">geopolitical</a> <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasus" class="mw-redirect" title="Transcaucasus">Transcaucasus</a> (South <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>) region, that is located in the Southern <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a> and their lowlands between the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>, and northeast of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Highland" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Highland">Armenian Highlands</a>. Located in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-classification_of_world_regions_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-classification_of_world_regions-16">[15]</a></sup> on the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Highlands" title="Armenian Highlands">Armenian Highlands</a>, it is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> to the north, the <a href="/wiki/Lachin_corridor" title="Lachin corridor">Lachin corridor</a> which is a part of <a href="/wiki/Lachin_District" title="Lachin District">Lachin District</a> that is under the control of a Russian peacekeeping force and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> proper to the east, and <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and Azerbaijan's <a href="/wiki/Exclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclave">exclave</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nakhchivan_Autonomous_Republic" title="Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic">Nakhchivan</a> to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-Oxford_University_Press_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford_University_Press-18">[17]</a></sup> Armenia lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/38th_parallel_north" title="38th parallel north">38°</a> and <a href="/wiki/42nd_parallel_north" title="42nd parallel north">42° N</a>, and meridians <a href="/wiki/43rd_meridian_east" title="43rd meridian east">43°</a> and <a href="/wiki/47th_meridian_east" title="47th meridian east">47° E</a>. It contains two terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_mixed_forests" title="Caucasus mixed forests">Caucasus mixed forests</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Anatolian_montane_steppe" title="Eastern Anatolian montane steppe">Eastern Anatolian montane steppe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-112">[111]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Armenien_topo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Armenien_topo.jpg/220px-Armenien_topo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Armenien_topo.jpg/330px-Armenien_topo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Armenien_topo.jpg/440px-Armenien_topo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1314"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Armenien_topo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Armenia's mountainous and volcanic <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topography</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenia has a territorial area of 29,743 square kilometres (11,484&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). The terrain is mostly mountainous, with fast flowing rivers, and few forests. The land rises to 4,090 metres (13,419 feet) <a href="/wiki/Metres_above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Metres above sea level">above sea level</a> at <a href="/wiki/Mount_Aragats" title="Mount Aragats">Mount Aragats</a>, and no point is below 390 metres (1,280&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Metres_above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Metres above sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_average_elevation" title="List of countries by average elevation">Average elevation of the country</a> area is 10th highest in the world and it has 85.9% mountain area, more than <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> or <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Mount Ararat
       </dt>
      </dl> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Mount_Ararat" title="Mount Ararat">Mount Ararat</a>, which was historically part of Armenia, is the highest mountain in the region at 5,137 meters (16,854 feet). Now located in Turkey, but clearly visible from Armenia, it is regarded by the Armenians as a symbol of their land. Because of this, the mountain is present on the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Armenia" title="Coat of arms of Armenia">Armenian national emblem</a> today.<sup id="cite_ref-Azarian2007_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Azarian2007-115">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Adalian2010_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adalian2010-116">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Minahan1998_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan1998-117">[116]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Armenia" title="Climate of Armenia">Climate of Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_ARM_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Koppen-Geiger_Map_ARM_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_ARM_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Koppen-Geiger_Map_ARM_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_ARM_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Koppen-Geiger_Map_ARM_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_ARM_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1455" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_ARM_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen-Geiger_climate_classification" class="mw-redirect" title="Köppen-Geiger climate classification">Köppen-Geiger climate classification</a> map for Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The climate in Armenia is markedly highland <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental</a>. Summers are hot, dry and sunny, lasting from June to mid-September. The temperature fluctuates between 22 and 36&nbsp;°C (72 and 97&nbsp;°F). However, the low humidity level mitigates the effect of high temperatures. Evening breezes blowing down the mountains provide a welcome refreshing and cooling effect. Springs are short, while autumns are long. Autumns are known for their vibrant and colourful foliage. </p>
      <p>Winters are quite cold with plenty of snow, with temperatures ranging between −10 and −5&nbsp;°C (14 and 23&nbsp;°F). <a href="/wiki/Winter_sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter sport">Winter sports</a> enthusiasts enjoy skiing down the hills of <a href="/wiki/Tsakhkadzor" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsakhkadzor">Tsakhkadzor</a>, located thirty minutes outside Yerevan. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Sevan" title="Lake Sevan">Lake Sevan</a>, nestled up in the Armenian highlands, is the second largest lake in the world relative to its altitude, at 1,900 metres (6,234&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Metres_above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Metres above sea level">above sea level</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia,_Azerbaijan,_Georgia,_Russia,_Germany,_Italy,_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg/220px-CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg/330px-CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg/440px-CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia%2C_Azerbaijan%2C_Georgia%2C_Russia%2C_Germany%2C_Italy%2C_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="658" data-file-height="362"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CO2_emissions_per_capita_in_Armenia,_Azerbaijan,_Georgia,_Russia,_Germany,_Italy,_USA_in_2000-2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Carbon dioxide emissions in metric tons per capita in Armenia, Azerbaijan, Georgia, Russia, Germany, Italy, USA in 2000–2012. World Bank data.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenia ranked 63rd out of 180 countries on <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a> (EPI) in 2018. Its rank on subindex Environmental Health (which is weighted at 40% in EPI) is 109, while Armenia's rank on subindex of Ecosystem Vitality (weighted at 60% in EPI) is 27th best in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> This suggests that main environmental issues in Armenia are with <a href="/wiki/Armenia#Health" title="Armenia">population health</a>, while environment vitality is of lesser concern. Out of sub-subindices contributing to Environmental Health subindex ranking on Air Quality to which population is exposed is particularly unsatisfying. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Waste_management_in_Armenia" title="Waste management in Armenia">Waste management in Armenia</a> is underdeveloped, as no waste sorting or recycling takes place at Armenia's 60 landfills. A waste processing plant is scheduled for construction near <a href="/wiki/Hrazdan" title="Hrazdan">Hrazdan</a> city, which will allow for closure of 10 waste dumps.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite the availability of abundant renewable energy sources in Armenia (especially <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>) and calls from EU officials to shut down the <a href="/wiki/Metsamor_Nuclear_Power_Plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Metsamor Nuclear Power Plant">nuclear power plant at Metsamor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> the Armenian Government is exploring the possibilities of installing new small modular nuclear reactors. In 2018 existing nuclear plant is scheduled for modernization to enhance its safety and increase power production by about 10%.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Armenia" title="Government of Armenia">Government of Armenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Armenia" title="Politics of Armenia">Politics of Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2014_Erywa%C5%84,_Budynek_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_Republiki_Armenii.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/2014_Erywa%C5%84%2C_Budynek_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_Republiki_Armenii.jpg/220px-2014_Erywa%C5%84%2C_Budynek_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_Republiki_Armenii.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/2014_Erywa%C5%84%2C_Budynek_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_Republiki_Armenii.jpg/330px-2014_Erywa%C5%84%2C_Budynek_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_Republiki_Armenii.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/2014_Erywa%C5%84%2C_Budynek_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_Republiki_Armenii.jpg/440px-2014_Erywa%C5%84%2C_Budynek_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_Republiki_Armenii.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2412"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2014_Erywa%C5%84,_Budynek_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_Republiki_Armenii.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Armenia)" title="National Assembly (Armenia)">National Assembly</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenia is a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative parliamentary democratic</a> republic. The Armenian constitution adhered to the model of a <a href="/wiki/Semi-Presidential_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-Presidential Republic">semi-presidential republic</a> until April 2018. </p>
      <p>According to the current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Armenia" title="Constitution of Armenia">Constitution of Armenia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Armenia" title="President of Armenia">President</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> holding largely representational functions, while the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Armenia" title="Prime Minister of Armenia">Prime Minister</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and exercises <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">Legislative power</a> is vested in the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Armenia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Armenia">Azgayin Zhoghov</a> or <i><a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Armenia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Armenia">National Assembly</a></i>, which is a <a href="/wiki/Unicameral_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral parliament">unicameral parliament</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Fragile_States_Index" title="Fragile States Index">Fragile states index</a> since its first report in 2006 until most recent in 2019 consistently ranked Armenia better than all its neighboring countries (with one exception in 2011).<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Armenia has universal <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffrage</a> above the age of eighteen. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Armenia" title="Foreign relations of Armenia">Foreign relations of Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenia_and_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenia and the European Union">Armenia and the European Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armenia%E2%80%93Turkey_relations" title="Armenia–Turkey relations">Armenia–Turkey relations</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Armen_Sarkissian_with_Mike_Pompeo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Armen_Sarkissian_with_Mike_Pompeo.jpg/220px-Armen_Sarkissian_with_Mike_Pompeo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Armen_Sarkissian_with_Mike_Pompeo.jpg/330px-Armen_Sarkissian_with_Mike_Pompeo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Armen_Sarkissian_with_Mike_Pompeo.jpg/440px-Armen_Sarkissian_with_Mike_Pompeo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5017" data-file-height="3345"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Armen_Sarkissian_with_Mike_Pompeo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>U.S. Secretary <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pompeo" title="Mike Pompeo">Mike Pompeo</a> with Armenian President <a href="/wiki/Armen_Sarksyan" title="Armen Sarksyan">Armen Sarksyan</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenia became a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> on 2 March 1992, and is a signatory to a number of its organizations and other international agreements. It is also a member of international organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="European Bank for Reconstruction and Development">European Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Customs_Organization" title="World Customs Organization">World Customs Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_the_Black_Sea_Economic_Cooperation" title="Organization of the Black Sea Economic Cooperation">Organization of the Black Sea Economic Cooperation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Security Treaty Organisation">CSTO</a> military alliance, and also participates in <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> program and the <a href="/wiki/Euro-Atlantic_Partnership_Council" title="Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council">Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council</a>. In 2004 its forces joined <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">KFOR</a>, a NATO-led international force in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>. Armenia is also an observer member of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Armenia_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Armenia-125">[124]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Alliance" title="Pacific Alliance">Pacific Alliance</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, and a dialogue partner in the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">Shanghai Cooperation Organisation</a>. As a result of its historical ties to France, Armenia was selected to host the biennial <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Francophonie summit</a> in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Armenia has a difficult relation with neighbouring countries <a href="/wiki/Armenia%E2%80%93Azerbaijan_relations" title="Armenia–Azerbaijan relations">Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenia%E2%80%93Turkey_relations" title="Armenia–Turkey relations">Turkey</a>. Tensions were running high between Armenians and Azerbaijanis during the final years of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_conflict" title="Nagorno-Karabakh conflict">Nagorno-Karabakh conflict</a> dominated the region's politics throughout the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-CFR-9148_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CFR-9148-127">[126]</a></sup> To this day, Armenia's borders with Turkey and Azerbaijan are under severe blockade. In addition, a permanent solution for the Nagorno-Karabakh conflict has not been reached despite the mediation provided by organizations such as the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>. </p>
      <p>Turkey also has a long history of poor relations with Armenia over its refusal to acknowledge the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian Genocide</a>, even though it was one of the first countries to recognize the Republic of Armenia (the 3rd republic) after its independence from the USSR in 1991. Despite this, for most of the 20th century and early 21st century, relations remain tense and there are no formal diplomatic relations between the two countries due to Turkey's refusal to establish them for numerous reasons. During the first Nagorno-Karabakh War, and citing it as the reason, Turkey closed its border with Armenia in 1993. It has not lifted its blockade despite pressure from the powerful Turkish business lobby interested in Armenian markets.<sup id="cite_ref-CFR-9148_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CFR-9148-127">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Nikol_Pashinyan_(2018-05-14)_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Vladimir_Putin_and_Nikol_Pashinyan_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Nikol_Pashinyan_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Vladimir_Putin_and_Nikol_Pashinyan_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Nikol_Pashinyan_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Vladimir_Putin_and_Nikol_Pashinyan_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Nikol_Pashinyan_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Nikol_Pashinyan_(2018-05-14)_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> shakes hands with Armenian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Nikol_Pashinyan" title="Nikol Pashinyan">Nikol Pashinyan</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 10 October 2009, Armenia and Turkey <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Protocols" title="Zurich Protocols">signed protocols</a> on the normalisation of relations, which set a timetable for restoring diplomatic ties and reopening their joint border.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> The ratification of those had to be made in the national parliaments. In Armenia, before sending the protocols to the parliament, it was sent to the Constitutional Court to have their <a href="/wiki/Constitutionality" title="Constitutionality">constitutionality</a> to be approved. The Constitutional Court made references to the preamble of the protocols underlying three main issues.<sup id="cite_ref-iaireport_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iaireport-129">[128]</a></sup> One of them stated that the implementation of the protocols did not imply Armenia's official recognition of the existing Turkish-Armenian border established by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kars" title="Treaty of Kars">Treaty of Kars</a>. By doing so, the Constitutional Court rejected one of the main premises of the protocols, i.e. “the mutual recognition of the existing border between the two countries as defined by relevant treaties of international law".<sup id="cite_ref-iaireport_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iaireport-129">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> This was for the Turkish Government the reason to back down from the Protocols.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> The Armenian President had made multiple public announcements, both in Armenia and abroad, that, as the leader of the political majority of Armenia, he assured the parliamentary ratification of the protocols if Turkey also ratified them. Despite this, the process stopped, as Turkey continuously added more preconditions to its ratification and also "delayed it beyond any reasonable time-period".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Unclear which preconditions were added by Turkey (June 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Due to its position between two unfriendly neighbours, Armenia has close security ties with Russia. At the request of the Armenian government, Russia maintains a <a href="/wiki/Russian_102nd_Military_Base" title="Russian 102nd Military Base">military base</a> in the city of <a href="/wiki/Gyumri" title="Gyumri">Gyumri</a> located in Northwestern Armenia<sup id="cite_ref-Armenia-base_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Armenia-base-132">[131]</a></sup> as a deterrent against Turkey.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Despite this, Armenia has also been looking toward Euro-Atlantic structures in recent years. It maintains good relations with the United States especially through its <a href="/wiki/Armenian_diaspora" title="Armenian diaspora">Armenian diaspora</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census" title="United States Census">US Census Bureau</a>, there are 427,822 Armenians living in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-2.jpg/220px-Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-2.jpg/330px-Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-2.jpg/440px-Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_at_Armenian_Genocide_memorial-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Russian President <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> at <a href="/wiki/Tsitsernakaberd" title="Tsitsernakaberd">Armenian Genocide memorial</a> in Yerevan.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Because of the illicit border blockades by Azerbaijan and Turkey, Armenia continues to maintain solid relations with its southern neighbour Iran especially in the economic sector. Economic projects are being developed between the two nations, including a gas pipeline going from Iran to Armenia. </p>
      <p>Armenia is a member of the Council of Europe and maintains friendly relations with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>; especially with its member states such as France and Greece. In January 2002, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> noted that Armenia may enter the EU in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> A 2005 survey reported that 64% of Armenia's population would be in favour of joining the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> Several Armenian officials have also expressed the desire for their country to eventually become an EU member state,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (January 2016)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> predicting that it will make an official bid for membership in a few years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Armenian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian SSR">A former republic</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, Armenia is an <a href="/wiki/Emergent_democracy" title="Emergent democracy">emerging democracy</a> and as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> was negotiating with the European Union to become an associate partner. Legally speaking, it has the right to be considered as a prospective EU member provided it meets necessary standards and criteria, although officially such a plan does not exist in Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> The Government of Armenia, however, has joined the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Customs_Union" title="Eurasian Customs Union">Eurasian Customs Union</a><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurasian Union">Eurasian Economic Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Armenia is included in the European Union's <a href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy" title="European Neighbourhood Policy">European Neighbourhood Policy</a> (ENP) and participates in both the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Partnership" title="Eastern Partnership">Eastern Partnership</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Euronest_Parliamentary_Assembly" title="Euronest Parliamentary Assembly">Euronest Parliamentary Assembly</a>, which aims at bringing the EU and its neighbours closer. The <a href="/wiki/Armenia-EU_Comprehensive_and_Enhanced_Partnership_Agreement" title="Armenia-EU Comprehensive and Enhanced Partnership Agreement">Armenia-EU Comprehensive and Enhanced Partnership Agreement</a> (CEPA) was signed on 24 November 2017. The agreement further develops cooperation in economic, trade and political areas, aims to improve investment climate, and is designed to bring Armenian law gradually closer to the <a href="/wiki/Acquis_communautaire" title="Acquis communautaire">EU acquis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-145">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Armenia" title="Armed Forces of Armenia">Armed Forces of Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Armenia" title="Military history of Armenia">Military history of Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_Air_force_(896484593).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Armenian_Air_force_%28896484593%29.jpg/220px-Armenian_Air_force_%28896484593%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Armenian_Air_force_%28896484593%29.jpg/330px-Armenian_Air_force_%28896484593%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Armenian_Air_force_%28896484593%29.jpg/440px-Armenian_Air_force_%28896484593%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="347"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_Air_force_(896484593).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Armenian_Air_Force" title="Armenian Air Force">Armenian Air Force</a> <a href="/wiki/Su-25" class="mw-redirect" title="Su-25">Su-25</a>'s during a military parade.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Army">Armenian Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Air_Force" title="Armenian Air Force">Air Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Air_Force" title="Armenian Air Force">Air Defence</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Border_Guard" title="Armenian Border Guard">Border Guard</a> comprise the four branches of the Armed Forces of Armenia. The Armenian military was formed after the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1985%E2%80%9391)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Soviet Union (1985–91)">collapse of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991 and with the establishment of the Ministry of Defence in 1992. The <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander-in-Chief</a> of the military is the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Armenia" title="Prime Minister of Armenia">Prime Minister of Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikol_Pashinyan" title="Nikol Pashinyan">Nikol Pashinyan</a>. The Ministry of Defence is in charge of political leadership, headed by <a href="/wiki/David_Tonoyan" title="David Tonoyan">Davit Tonoyan</a>, while military command remains in the hands of the general staff, headed by the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_General_Staff_(Armenia)" title="Chief of the General Staff (Armenia)">Chief of Staff</a>, who is Lieutenant-General <a href="/wiki/Onik_Gasparyan" title="Onik Gasparyan">Onik Gasparyan</a>. </p>
      <p>Active forces now number about 81,000 soldiers, with an additional <a href="/wiki/Military_reserve_force" title="Military reserve force">reserve</a> of 32,000 troops. Armenian border guards are in charge of patrolling the country's borders with <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, while Russian troops continue to monitor its borders with <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. In the case of an attack, Armenia is able to mobilize every able-bodied man between the age of 15 and 59, with military preparedness.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_Conventional_Armed_Forces_in_Europe" title="Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe">Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe</a>, which establishes comprehensive limits on key categories of military equipment, was ratified by the Armenian parliament in July 1992. In March 1993, Armenia signed the multilateral <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Weapons_Convention" title="Chemical Weapons Convention">Chemical Weapons Convention</a>, which calls for the eventual elimination of chemical weapons. Armenia acceded to the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Non-Proliferation_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty">Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty</a> (NPT) as a non-nuclear weapons state in July 1993. Armenia is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Security Treaty Organisation">Collective Security Treaty Organisation</a> (CSTO). Armenia also has an <a href="/wiki/Individual_Partnership_Action_Plan" title="Individual Partnership Action Plan">Individual Partnership Action Plan</a> with <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and it participates in NATO's <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> (PiP) program and the <a href="/wiki/Euro-Atlantic_Partnership_Council" title="Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council">Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council</a> (EAPC). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights_and_freedom">Human rights and freedom</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Armenia" title="Human rights in Armenia">Human rights in Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Raffi-kojian_20180423_190358284.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Raffi-kojian_20180423_190358284.jpg/220px-Raffi-kojian_20180423_190358284.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Raffi-kojian_20180423_190358284.jpg/330px-Raffi-kojian_20180423_190358284.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Raffi-kojian_20180423_190358284.jpg/440px-Raffi-kojian_20180423_190358284.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Raffi-kojian_20180423_190358284.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>In April 2018, a quasi-authoritarian <a href="/wiki/Serzh_Sargsyan" title="Serzh Sargsyan">regime</a> collapsed as a result of a nationwide <a href="/wiki/2018_Armenian_revolution" title="2018 Armenian revolution">protest movement in Armenia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Human rights in Armenia tend to be better than those in most <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">former Soviet republics</a> and have drawn closer to acceptable standards, especially economically.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Nonetheless, there are still several considerable problems. </p>
      <p>Armenia scored 4.79 on <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">The Economist Intelligence Unit</a> <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit#Democracy_Index" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Democracy Index</a> published in January 2019 (data for 2018). Although still classified as "<a href="/wiki/Hybrid_regime" title="Hybrid regime">hybrid regime</a>", Armenia recorded the strongest improvement among European countries<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> and reached its ever-best score since calculation began in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Armenia is classified as "partly free" in the 2019 report (with data from 2018) by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>, which gives it a score of 51 out of 100,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> which is 6 points ahead of the previous estimate.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Armenia has recorded an unprecedented progress in the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">World Press Freedom Index</a> published by <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>, improving its position by 19 points and ranking 61st on the list. The publication also confirms the absence of cases of killed journalists, citizen journalists or media assistants.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Armenia ranks 54th in the 2017 report The Human Freedom Index (with data from 2016) published by Canada's <a href="/wiki/Fraser_Institute" title="Fraser Institute">Fraser Institute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Armenia ranked 29th for economic freedom and 76th for personal freedom among 159 countries in the 2017 <a href="/wiki/List_of_freedom_indices" title="List of freedom indices">Human Freedom Index</a> published by the <a href="/wiki/Cato_Institute" title="Cato Institute">Cato Institute</a> .<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>These classifications may improve when data from 2018, including the period of the <a href="/wiki/2018_Armenian_Velvet_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="2018 Armenian Velvet Revolution">velvet revolution</a> and thereafter, is analyzed. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>

       <div style="position:absolute; left:302px; top:290px">
        <a href="/wiki/Syunik_Province" title="Syunik Province">Syunik</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg/220px-%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg/330px-%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg/440px-%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4161" data-file-height="2747"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D4%B3%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A1%D6%80%D5%A4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Geghard" title="Geghard">Geghard</a> monastery, <a href="/wiki/Kotayk_Province" title="Kotayk Province">Kotayk Province</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenia is divided into ten <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Armenia" title="Administrative divisions of Armenia">provinces</a> (<i>marzer</i>, singular <i>marz</i>), with the city (<i>kaghak</i>) of <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a> (<span lang="hy" title="Armenian-language text">Երևան</span>) having special administrative status as the country's capital. The chief executive in each of the ten provinces is the <i>marzpet</i> (<i>marz</i> governor), appointed by the government of Armenia. In Yerevan, the chief executive is the mayor, elected since 2009. </p>
      <p>Within each province there are <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_of_Armenia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of municipalities of Armenia">communities</a> (<i>hamaynkner</i>, singular <i>hamaynk</i>). Each community is self-governing and consists of one or more settlements (<i>bnakavayrer</i>, singular <i>bnakavayr</i>). Settlements are classified as either towns (<i>kaghakner</i>, singular <i>kaghak</i>) or villages (<i>gyugher</i>, singular <i>gyugh</i>). As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Armenia includes 915 communities, of which 49 are considered urban and 866 are considered rural. The capital, Yerevan, also has the status of a community.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> Additionally, Yerevan is divided into twelve semi-autonomous districts. </p>
