      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Armenia" title="Economy of Armenia">Economy of Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The economy relies heavily on investment and support from Armenians abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> Before independence, Armenia's economy was largely industry-based – <a href="/wiki/Chemical_substance" title="Chemical substance">chemicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>, machinery, <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">processed food</a>, <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_rubber" title="Synthetic rubber">synthetic rubber</a>, and textile – and highly dependent on outside resources. The republic had developed a modern <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">industrial sector</a>, supplying <a href="/wiki/Machine_tool" title="Machine tool">machine tools</a>, textiles, and other <a href="/wiki/Final_goods" class="mw-redirect" title="Final goods">manufactured goods</a> to sister republics in exchange for raw materials and energy.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-62">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Agriculture accounted for less than 20% of both <a href="/wiki/Net_material_product" title="Net material product">net material product</a> and <a href="/wiki/Full_employment" title="Full employment">total employment</a> before the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1985%E2%80%931991)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Soviet Union (1985–1991)">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991. After independence, the importance of agriculture in the economy increased markedly, its share at the end of the 1990s rising to more than 30% of GDP and more than 40% of total employment.<sup id="cite_ref-agri_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agri-159">[158]</a></sup> This increase in the importance of agriculture was attributable to food security needs of the population in the face of uncertainty during the first phases of <a href="/wiki/Transition_economy" title="Transition economy">transition</a> and the collapse of the non-agricultural sectors of the economy in the early 1990s. As the economic situation stabilised and growth resumed, the share of agriculture in GDP dropped to slightly over 20% (2006 data), although the share of agriculture in employment remained more than 40%.<sup id="cite_ref-yb2007_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yb2007-160">[159]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg/220px-Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg/330px-Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg/440px-Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mount_Ararat_and_the_Yerevan_skyline.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a> is the economic and cultural centre of Armenia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenian mines produce copper, zinc, gold, and lead. The vast majority of energy is produced with fuel imported from Russia, including gas and nuclear fuel (for its one nuclear power plant); the main domestic energy source is hydroelectric. Small deposits of coal, gas, and petroleum exist but have not yet been developed. </p>
      <p>Access to <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> in Armenia is lower than world average. In 2016, Armenia had 0.8 global hectares <sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-161">[160]</a></sup> of biocapacity per person within its territory, much less than the world average of 1.6 global hectares per person.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup> In 2016 Armenia used 1.9 global hectares of biocapacity per person - their <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> of consumption. This means they use double as much biocapacity as Armenia contains. As a result, Armenia is running a biocapacity deficit.<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-161">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Like other <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">newly independent states</a> of the former Soviet Union, Armenia's economy suffers from the breakdown of former Soviet trading patterns. Soviet investment in and support of Armenian industry has virtually disappeared, so that few major enterprises are still able to function. In addition, the effects of the <a href="/wiki/1988_Armenian_earthquake" title="1988 Armenian earthquake">1988 Spitak earthquake</a>, which killed more than 25,000 people and made 500,000 homeless, are still being felt. The conflict with Azerbaijan over Nagorno-Karabakh has not been resolved. Shutdown of the nuclear power plant in 1989 lead to the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_energy_crisis_of_1990s" title="Armenian energy crisis of 1990s">Armenian energy crisis of 1990s</a>. The GDP fell nearly 60% between 1989 and 1993, but then resumed robust growth after the power plant was reopened in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-agri_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agri-159">[158]</a></sup> The national currency, the dram, suffered hyperinflation for the first years after its introduction in 1993. </p>
      <p>Nevertheless, the government was able to make wide-ranging economic reforms that paid off in dramatically lower inflation and steady growth. The 1994 cease-fire in the Nagorno-Karabakh conflict has also helped the economy. Armenia has had strong economic growth since 1995, building on the turnaround that began the previous year, and inflation has been negligible for the past several years. New sectors, such as precious-stone processing and jewelry making, information and communication technology and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Armenia" title="Tourism in Armenia">tourism</a> are beginning to supplement more traditional sectors of the economy, such as agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>This steady economic progress has earned Armenia increasing support from international institutions. The <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="European Bank for Reconstruction and Development">European Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a> (EBRD), and other <a href="/wiki/Global_financial_system" title="Global financial system">international financial institutions</a> (IFIs) and foreign countries are extending considerable grants and loans. Loans to Armenia since 1993 exceed $1.1&nbsp;billion. These loans are targeted at reducing the budget deficit and stabilising the currency; developing private businesses; energy; agriculture; food processing; transportation; the health and education sectors; and ongoing rehabilitation in the earthquake zone. The government joined the World Trade Organization on 5 February 2003. But one of the main sources of foreign direct investments remains the Armenian diaspora, which finances major parts of the reconstruction of infrastructure and other public projects. Being a growing democratic state, Armenia also hopes to get more financial aid from the Western World. </p>
      <p>A liberal foreign investment law was approved in June 1994, and a law on privatization was adopted in 1997, as well as a program of state property privatization. Continued progress will depend on the ability of the government to strengthen its macroeconomic management, including increasing revenue collection, improving the investment climate, and making strides against corruption. However, unemployment, which was 18.5% in 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup> still remains a major problem due to the influx of thousands of refugees from the Karabakh conflict. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_rankings">International rankings</span></h3> 
      <p>In the 2021 report of <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a> by <a href="/wiki/The_Heritage_Foundation" title="The Heritage Foundation">Heritage Foundation</a>, Armenia is classified as "mostly free" and ranks 32th, ahead of all other <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Union" title="Eurasian Economic Union">Eurasian Economic Union</a> countries and many <a href="/wiki/EU" class="mw-redirect" title="EU">EU</a> countries including Cyprus, Bulgaria, Romania, Poland, Belgium, Spain, France, Portugal and Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-economic-index_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economic-index-101">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 2019 report (data for 2017) of <a href="/wiki/Economic_Freedom_of_the_World" title="Economic Freedom of the World">Economic Freedom of the World</a> published by <a href="/wiki/Fraser_Institute" title="Fraser Institute">Fraser Institute</a> Armenia ranks 27th (classified most free) out of 162 economies.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 2019 report of <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Competitiveness Index">Global Competitiveness Index</a> Armenia ranks 69th out of 141 economies.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 2020 report (data for 2019) of <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">Doing Business</a> Index Armenia ranks 47th with 10th rank on "starting business" sub-index.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 2018 report (data for 2017) of <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> by <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UNDP</a> Armenia ranked 83rd and is classified into "high human development" group.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 2020 report of <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a> by <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a> Armenia ranked 49 of 179 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the "Freedom on the Net 2019" report by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> Armenia scored best in the region and was classified as a free country.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span id="Science.2C_technology_and_education"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Science,_technology_and_education">Science, technology and education</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Armenia" title="Science and technology in Armenia">Science and technology in Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Research spending is low in Armenia, averaging 0.25% of GDP over 2010–2013. However, the statistical record of research expenditure is incomplete, as expenditure by privately owned business enterprises is not surveyed in Armenia. The world average for domestic expenditure on research was 1.7% of GDP in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-174">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries,_2001%E2%80%932013.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg/220px-GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg/330px-GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg/440px-GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries%2C_2001%E2%80%932013.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="486"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GERD_GDP_ratio_for_the_Black_Sea_countries,_2001%E2%80%932013.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Gross domestic expenditure on R&amp;D (GERD)to GDP ratio for the Black Sea countries, 2001–2013. Source: UNESCO Science Report: towards 2030 (2015), Figure 12.3
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country's <i>Strategy for the Development of Science 2011–2020</i> envisions that 'by 2020, Armenia is a country with a knowledge-based economy and is competitive within the European Research Area with its level of basic and applied research.' It fixes the following targets:<sup id="cite_ref-:0_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-174">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Creation of a system capable of sustaining the development of science and technology;</li> 
       <li>Development of scientific potential, modernization of scientific infrastructure;</li> 
       <li>Promotion of basic and applied research;</li> 
       <li>Creation of a synergistic system of education, science and innovation; and</li> 
       <li>Becoming a prime location for scientific specialization in the European Research Area.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Based on this strategy, the accompanying <i>Action Plan</i> was approved by the government in June 2011. It defines the following targets:<sup id="cite_ref-:0_174-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-174">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Improve the management system for science and technology and create the requisite conditions for sustainable development;</li> 
       <li>Involve more young, talented people in education and research, while upgrading research infrastructure;</li> 
       <li>Create the requisite conditions for the development of an integrated national innovation system; and</li> 
       <li>Enhance international co-operation in research and development.</li>
      </ul> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance,_2005_and_2013.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg/220px-GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg/330px-GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg/440px-GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance%2C_2005_and_2013.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="633"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GERD_in_the_Black_Sea_region_by_sector_of_performance,_2005_and_2013.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>GERD in the Black Sea region by sector of performance, 2005 and 2013. Source: UNESCO Science Report: towards 2030 (2015), Figure 12.5
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although the <i>Strategy</i> clearly pursues a 'science push' approach, with public research institutes serving as the key policy target, it nevertheless mentions the goal of establishing an innovation system. However, the main driver of innovation, the business sector, is not mentioned. In between publishing the <i>Strategy</i> and <i>Action Plan</i>, the government issued a resolution in May 2010 on <i>Science and Technology Development Priorities for 2010–2014</i>. These priorities are:<sup id="cite_ref-:0_174-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-174">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Armenian studies, humanities and social sciences;</li> 
       <li>Life sciences;</li> 
       <li>Renewable energy, new energy sources;</li> 
       <li>Advanced technologies, information technologies;</li> 
       <li>Space, Earth sciences, sustainable use of natural resources; and</li> 
       <li>Basic research promoting essential applied research.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The Law on the National Academy of Sciences was adopted in May 2011. This law is expected to play a key role in shaping the Armenian innovation system. It allows the National Academy of Sciences to extend its business activities to the commercialization of research results and the creation of spin-offs; it also makes provision for restructuring the National Academy of Sciences by combining institutes involved in closely related research areas into a single body. Three of these new centres are particularly relevant: the Centre for Biotechnology, the Centre for Zoology and Hydro-ecology and the Centre for Organic and Pharmaceutical Chemistry.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_174-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-174">[173]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government is focusing its support on selected industrial sectors. More than 20 projects have been cofunded by the State Committee of Science in targeted branches: pharmaceuticals, medicine and biotechnology, agricultural mechanization and machine building, electronics, engineering, chemistry and, in particular, the sphere of information technology.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_174-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-174">[173]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Over the past decade, the government has made an effort to encourage science–industry linkages. The Armenian information technology sector has been particularly active: a number of public–private partnerships have been established between companies and universities, in order to give students marketable skills and generate innovative ideas at the interface of science and business. Examples are Synopsys Inc. and the Enterprise Incubator Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_174-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-174">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Old_building_of_Yerevan_State_University2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Old_building_of_Yerevan_State_University2.jpg/220px-Old_building_of_Yerevan_State_University2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Old_building_of_Yerevan_State_University2.jpg/330px-Old_building_of_Yerevan_State_University2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Old_building_of_Yerevan_State_University2.jpg/440px-Old_building_of_Yerevan_State_University2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Old_building_of_Yerevan_State_University2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Yerevan_State_University" title="Yerevan State University">Yerevan State University</a> building
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Armenia" title="Education in Armenia">Education in Armenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Armenia" title="List of universities in Armenia">List of universities in Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In medieval times, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Gladzor" title="University of Gladzor">University of Gladzor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tatev_Monastery#Tatev_University" title="Tatev Monastery">University of Tatev</a> took an important role for whole Armenia. </p>
      <p>A literacy rate of 100% was reported as early as 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic">In the communist era</a>, Armenian education followed the standard Soviet model of complete state control (from Moscow) of <a href="/wiki/Curriculum" title="Curriculum">curricula</a> and teaching methods and close integration of education activities with other aspects of society, such as politics, culture, and the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 1988–89 school year, 301 students per 10,000 were in specialized secondary or higher education, a figure slightly lower than the Soviet average.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> In 1989, some 58% of Armenians over age fifteen had completed their secondary education, and 14% had a higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> In the 1990–91 school year, the estimated 1,307 primary and secondary schools were attended by 608,800 students.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> Another seventy specialised secondary institutions had 45,900 students, and 68,400 students were enrolled in a total of ten postsecondary institutions that included universities.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> In addition, 35% of eligible children attended <a href="/wiki/Preschool_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Preschool education">preschools</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> In 1992 Armenia's largest institution of higher learning, <a href="/wiki/Yerevan_State_University" title="Yerevan State University">Yerevan State University</a>, had eighteen departments, including ones for social sciences, sciences, and law.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> Its faculty numbered about 1,300 teachers and its student population about 10,000 students.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Polytechnic_University_of_Armenia" title="National Polytechnic University of Armenia">National Polytechnic University of Armenia</a> is operating since 1933.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the early 1990s, Armenia made substantial changes to the centralised and regimented Soviet system.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> Because at least 98% of students in higher education were Armenian, curricula began to emphasise <a href="/wiki/History_of_Armenia" title="History of Armenia">Armenian history</a> and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a> became the dominant language of instruction, and many schools that had taught in Russian closed by the end of 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> Russian was still widely taught, however, as a second language.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2014, the National Program for Educational Excellence embarked on creating an internationally competitive and academically rigorous alternative educational program (the Araratian Baccalaureate) for Armenian schools and increasing the importance and status of the teacher's role in society.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Ministry of Education and Science is responsible for regulation of the sector. Primary and secondary education in Armenia is free, and completion of secondary school is compulsory.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_175-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-175">[174]</a></sup> Higher education in Armenia is harmonized with the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Process" title="Bologna Process">Bologna process</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Higher_Education_Area" title="European Higher Education Area">European Higher Education Area</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Armenian National Academy of Sciences">Armenian National Academy of Sciences</a> plays an important role in postgraduate education. </p>
      <p>Schooling takes 12 years in Armenia and breaks down into primary (4 years), middle (5 years) and high school (3 years). Schools engage a 10-grade mark system. The government also supports <a href="/wiki/List_of_Armenian_schools#Schools_outside_Armenia" title="List of Armenian schools">Armenian schools outside of Armenia</a>. </p>
      <p>Gross enrollment in <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_education" title="Tertiary education">tertiary education</a> at 44% in 2015 surpassed peer countries of the South Caucasus but remained below the average for Europe and Central Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup> However, public spending per student in tertiary education in GDP-ratio terms is one of the lowest for post-USSR countries (for which data was available).<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:left;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Armenia" title="Demographics of Armenia">Demographics of Armenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Armenien_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population pyramid 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenia has a population of 2,951,745 (2018 est.)<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-180">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-181">[180]</a></sup> and is the third most densely populated of the former Soviet republics.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> There has been a problem of <a href="/wiki/Population_decline" title="Population decline">population decline</a> due to elevated levels of <a href="/wiki/Emigration" title="Emigration">emigration</a> after the break-up of the <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">USSR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup> In the past years emigration levels have declined and some population growth is observed since 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ArmenianDiaspora.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/ArmenianDiaspora.png/220px-ArmenianDiaspora.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/ArmenianDiaspora.png/330px-ArmenianDiaspora.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/ArmenianDiaspora.png/440px-ArmenianDiaspora.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ArmenianDiaspora.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_diaspora" title="Armenian diaspora">Armenian population around the world</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenia has <a href="/wiki/Armenian_diaspora" title="Armenian diaspora">a relatively large external diaspora</a> (8&nbsp;million by some estimates, greatly exceeding the 3&nbsp;million population of Armenia itself), with communities existing across the globe. The largest Armenian communities outside of Armenia can be found in Russia, France, Iran, the United States, Georgia, Syria, Lebanon, Australia, Canada, Greece, Cyprus, Israel, Poland, Ukraine and Brazil. 40,000 to 70,000 Armenians still live in Turkey (mostly in and around <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>About 1,000 Armenians reside in the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Quarter" title="Armenian Quarter">Armenian Quarter</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Old_City_(Jerusalem)" title="Old City (Jerusalem)">Old City</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>, a remnant of a once-larger community.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup> Italy is home to the <a href="/wiki/San_Lazzaro_degli_Armeni" title="San Lazzaro degli Armeni">San Lazzaro degli Armeni</a>, an island located in the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Lagoon" title="Venetian Lagoon">Venetian Lagoon</a>, which is completely occupied by a monastery run by the <a href="/wiki/Mechitarists" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechitarists">Mechitarists</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Catholic_Church" title="Armenian Catholic Church">Armenian Catholic</a> congregation.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup> Approximately 139,000 Armenians live in the de facto independent country <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh">Republic of Artsakh</a> where they form a majority.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_distribution_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Armenian_distribution_map.png/220px-Armenian_distribution_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Armenian_distribution_map.png/330px-Armenian_distribution_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Armenian_distribution_map.png/440px-Armenian_distribution_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1742" data-file-height="920"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_distribution_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><b>Historical and modern distribution of Armenians.<br></b>Settlement area of Armenians in early 20th century:
         <br>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><span class="legend nowrap"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#967117; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;&gt;50%</span><span class="nowrap">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><span class="legend nowrap"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FFA700; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;25–50%</span><span class="nowrap">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><span class="legend nowrap"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FBEC5D; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;&lt;25%</span>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FF0000; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Armenian settlement area today.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ethnic <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a> make up 98.1% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Yazidi" class="mw-redirect" title="Yazidi">Yazidis</a> make up 1.2%, and Russians 0.4%. Other minorities include <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontic_Greeks" title="Pontic Greeks">Greeks</a> (usually called <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Greeks" title="Caucasus Greeks">Caucasus Greeks</a>), <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish people">Kurds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Armenia" title="History of the Jews in Armenia">Jews</a>. There are also smaller communities of <a href="/wiki/Vlachs" title="Vlachs">Vlachs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mordvins" title="Mordvins">Mordvins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Udi_people" title="Udi people">Udis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tat_people_(Caucasus)" title="Tat people (Caucasus)">Tats</a>. Minorities of <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Germans" title="Caucasus Germans">Caucasus Germans</a> also exist though they are heavily <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russified</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-minorities_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minorities-189">[188]</a></sup> As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there are an estimated 35,000 Yazidis in Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-190">[189]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet era">Soviet era</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azerbaijanis</a> were historically the second largest population in the country (forming about 2.5% in 1989).<sup id="cite_ref-1989census_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1989census-191">[190]</a></sup> However, due to the conflict over <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a>, virtually all of them emigrated from Armenia to Azerbaijan. Conversely, Armenia received a large influx of Armenian refugees from Azerbaijan, thus giving Armenia a more homogeneous character. </p>
      <p>According to Gallup research conducted in 2017 Armenia has one of the highest migrant acceptance (welcoming) rates in eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Armenia" title="Languages of Armenia">Languages of Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a> is the only official language. The main foreign languages that Armenians know are Russian and English. Due to its Soviet past, most of the old population can speak Russian quite well. According to a 2013 survey, 95% of Armenians said they had some knowledge of Russian (24% advanced, 59% intermediate) compared to 40% who said they knew some English (4% advanced, 16% intermediate and 20% beginner). However, more adults (50%) think that English should be taught in public secondary schools than those who prefer Russian (44%).<sup id="cite_ref-2012_knowledge_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012_knowledge-193">[192]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities">Cities</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Armenia" title="Municipalities of Armenia">Municipalities of Armenia</a>
      </div>

          <div style="height:2.6em;line-height:1.3em;">
           <span style="font-size:110%;">Largest cities or towns in Armenia</span>
           <br>
           <div style="display:inline;font-weight:normal;">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Armenia" title="Religion in Armenia">Religion in Armenia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:PortalEchmiazin1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/PortalEchmiazin1.jpg/220px-PortalEchmiazin1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="447" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/PortalEchmiazin1.jpg/330px-PortalEchmiazin1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/PortalEchmiazin1.jpg/440px-PortalEchmiazin1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="4063"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:PortalEchmiazin1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Portal to the <i>Holy City</i> at Echmiazin, the seat of the Catholicos
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kohrvirab.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kohrvirab.jpg/220px-Kohrvirab.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kohrvirab.jpg/330px-Kohrvirab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kohrvirab.jpg/440px-Kohrvirab.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2334"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kohrvirab.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The 7th-century <a href="/wiki/Khor_Virap" title="Khor Virap">Khor Virap</a> monastery in the shadow of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Ararat" title="Mount Ararat">Mount Ararat</a>, the peak on which <a href="/wiki/Noah%27s_Ark" title="Noah's Ark">Noah's Ark</a> is said to have landed during the <a href="/wiki/Genesis_flood_narrative" title="Genesis flood narrative">biblical flood</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Armenia was the first nation to adopt <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> as a <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>, an event traditionally dated to AD 301.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The predominant <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Armenia" title="Religion in Armenia">religion in Armenia</a> is Christianity. Its roots go back to the 1st century AD, when it was founded by two of Jesus' twelve <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Apostles" class="mw-redirect" title="Twelve Apostles">apostles</a> – <a href="/wiki/Jude_the_Apostle" title="Jude the Apostle">Thaddaeus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_the_Apostle" title="Bartholomew the Apostle">Bartholomew</a> – who preached Christianity in Armenia between AD 40–60. </p>
      <p>Over 93% of Christians in Armenia belong to the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-census1_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census1-208">[207]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CI1A_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CI1A-209">[208]</a></sup> which is in communion only with the churches comprising <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodoxy#Oriental_Orthodox_Communion" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Orthodoxy">Oriental Orthodoxy</a>—of which it is itself a member. </p>
      <p>Catholics also exist in Armenia, both <a href="/wiki/Latin_Church" title="Latin Church">Latin rite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_rite" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian rite">Armenian rite</a>. The latter group, the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Catholic_Church" title="Armenian Catholic Church">Armenian Catholic Church</a>, is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Bzoummar" title="Bzoummar">Bzoummar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>. Of note are the <a href="/wiki/Mechitarists" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechitarists">Mechitarists</a> (also spelled "Mekhitarists" <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">Մխիթարեան</span>), a congregation of <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_Benedict" class="mw-redirect" title="Order of Saint Benedict">Benedictine</a> monks in the Armenian Catholic Church, founded in 1712 by <a href="/wiki/Mekhitar_of_Sebaste" class="mw-redirect" title="Mekhitar of Sebaste">Mekhitar of Sebaste</a>. They are best known for their series of scholarly publications of ancient <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenian</a> versions of otherwise lost ancient Greek texts. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Evangelical_Church" title="Armenian Evangelical Church">Armenian Evangelical Church</a> has several thousand members throughout the country. </p>
      <p>Other Christian denominations in Armenia are the Pentecostal branches of Protestant community such as the Word of Life, the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Brotherhood_Church" title="Armenian Brotherhood Church">Armenian Brotherhood Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[209]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> which are known as of the oldest existing denominations in Armenia and were permitted by the authorities of Soviet Union,<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Presbyterians" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterians">Presbyterians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Armenia is also home to a <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Armenia" title="Russians in Armenia">Russian</a> community of <a href="/wiki/Molokan" title="Molokan">Molokans</a> which practice a form of Spiritual Christianity originated from the Russian Orthodox Church.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Yazidis, who live in the western part of the country, practice <a href="/wiki/Yazidism" title="Yazidism">Yazidism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the world's largest Yazidi temple is under construction in the small village of Aknalish.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-190">[189]</a></sup> There are also Kurds who practice <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>There is a <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Armenia" title="History of the Jews in Armenia">Jewish community in Armenia</a> diminished to 750 persons since independence with most emigrants leaving for Israel. There are currently two synagogues in Armenia – in the capital, Yerevan, and in the city of <a href="/wiki/Sevan_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sevan (city)">Sevan</a> located near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Sevan" title="Lake Sevan">Lake Sevan</a>. </p>
